The Inconsistency of Transferring Divine Power
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazilite view on power transfer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that the Mu'tazilite concept of transferring God's power to creatures is logically inconsistent with God's power being essential.

Core Idea
Essential power cannot be transferred or diminished.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi directly challenges the Mu'tazilite position on divine power. They claim that God is powerful by His essence, yet also hold that God can 'empower' creatures to act, thereby losing power over those actions. Maturidi reveals the logical contradiction in this view, showing that an essential attribute cannot be removed or transferred. Let's unpack his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: it starts with an objection ('then it is said to him'), then presents the Mu'tazilite claim, and concludes with two impossible consequences.
Pay attention to the terms 'قدرة بالذات' (essential power) and 'العوارض' (accidents).
2
Identify the core contradiction
Find where Maturidi points out the inconsistency: the Mu'tazilites claim God is powerful by essence (which implies permanence) but then say His power can cease when He empowers creatures. This is the heart of the refutation.
3
Examine the two impossible conclusions
The passage ends with two statements labeled 'impossible' (محال). Understand why each follows logically from the Mu'tazilite view. The first: if power is essential yet no action appears, that is absurd. The second: if power can be removed, it cannot be essential.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the lesson for Islamic theology
Consider why Maturidi deems this argument important. It safeguards the concept of God's unique and unchanging nature. The Mu'tazilite view, if accepted, would imply change in God, which is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله: فيقال له: إذ هو قادر بنفسه لا بقدرة يعرض، كيف زعمتم أنه يقدر على خلق جميع حركات العباد وسكونهم إلى أن يقدرهم عليها؟ فإذا أقدرهم عليها زالت قدرته عليها إلا أن يأخذ القوة عنهم. فهذا وصف القدرة بالذات أو بالعوارض ومَنْ ذلك وصفه فالقول له بقوة لم يظهر منه الفعل محال؛ وما يحتمل زوال قدرته فالقول [له] بالقدرة بذاته على مذهبهم محال.
The jurist, may God have mercy on him, said: Then it is said to him: Since He is powerful by Himself, not by a power that is an accident, how can you claim that He is able to create all the movements and stillness of servants until He empowers them over them? Then when He empowers them over them, His power over them ceases unless He takes strength from them. This is a description of power by essence or by accidents, and whoever describes it thus, then the statement that He has a power from which no action appears is impossible; and whatever admits the removal of His power, then the statement that He has power by essence according to their school is impossible.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazilite position regarding God's power. The author argues that if God is powerful by His essence, as the Mu'tazilites claim, then His power cannot be transferred or diminished. Yet they claim that God empowers creatures to act, and thereby loses power over those actions. This is inconsistent: an essential power cannot be removed. The author points out that describing God's power as something that can cease makes it accidental, contradicting their own claim that it is by essence. Therefore, their view is self-contradictory.

Key Terms
قدرة بالذات (qudra bi-l-dhāt)
العوارض (al-‘awāriḍ)
إقدر (iqdār)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God can delegate His power to creatures, losing control over their actions.
Correction: Maturidi shows that if God's power is essential, it cannot be transferred or diminished. The Mu'tazilite view reduces essential power to accidental power, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
What is the central contradiction Maturidi identifies in the Mu'tazilite view?
A) They claim God is powerful by essence but then say His power can cease when He empowers creatures.
B) They deny that God has power.
C) They say God creates evil.
D) They claim power is an accident in God.

Key Takeaway
Essential divine power cannot be transferred or diminished; any view implying otherwise is logically inconsistent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever comfort yourself with the thought that God's power over that action has 'passed' or 'diminished'? How does this lesson expose that comfort as a dangerous illusion? Commit to recalling God's essential, unceasing power the next time you face temptation.
?
In what areas of your life—your career, relationships, or health—do you secretly believe God's power is limited, as if He 'empowers' you and then steps back? What would change if you truly lived knowing His power never recedes? Write down one area and a concrete act of trust.
?
You claim to believe that God's power is essential and never-ending. But when you worry about the future, your actions say otherwise. Will you repent today of treating God's power as something that can be exhausted? What is one practical step you will take to align your heart with this truth?

Refuting the Qadariyya's Questioning: Rational vs. Revealed
Imam Maturidi refutes the Qadariyya's method and states the principle of manifest divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qadariyya's theological method of questioning God's acts is invalid, as Imam Maturidi grounds the refutation in the distinction between rational and revealed knowledge.

Core Idea
Questioning God's acts based on transmitted evidence while the issue is rational is a category error.

Imam Maturidi begins by criticizing the Qadariyya sect for using a sensory-based answer (referring to acts of disbelief) to a rational question about the creation of actions. He then establishes a foundational principle: every creation manifests God's grace, generosity, wisdom, and oneness, making any 'why' question absurd.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the critique unfolds.
The passage is in two parts: first the error, then the principle.
2
Identify the two types of knowledge
Look for the terms 'sam'i' (revealed) and 'aqli' (rational). Understand how the Qadariyya misuse them.
The error is using a revealed answer for a rational question.
3
Understand the principle of manifest attributes
The shaykh states that every creation shows God's grace, generosity, wisdom, and proof of oneness. Reflect on why this makes questioning invalid.
If all creation already demonstrates His attributes, asking 'why' is redundant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى ذلك شأن القدرية فيما يُسألون عن خلق الأفعال، فيرجعون في الجواب إلى فعل الكفر والمعاصي. وذلك فاسد، لأن طريق هذا سمعي، والأول الذي وصف عقلي. قال الشيخ رحمه الله : والأصل عندنا أن الله تعالى لم يخلق خلقا إلا وأثر نعمه عليه ظاهر، وأدلة جوده فيه بين، وأن حكمته بما فيه من دلالة وحدانيته موجودة، وبرهان ونفاذ مشيئته فيه محقق، وعلامة قدرته وعلمه بحقائق الأشياء غير خفى في ذلك. والسؤال على أنك لم أنعمت أو لماذا أظهرت جودك، ولم كانت الحكمة، ولم أقمت حجة وحدانيتك ؟ إلى آخر ما ذكر محال فاسد لا يقبله عقل ولا يحتمله وسع لقبحه . لذلك بطل هذا النوع من السؤال. وبالله التوفيق. سلطانه ثم جائز أن يقال: إذ هو بذاته جواد، وبذاته قادر، وبذاته عالم فجاد بخلقه على خلقه؛ إذ هو خلقه، إذ هو قادر على أن يجود ويُظهر مواهبه. وأصل هذا السؤال عندنا فاسد، لأنا نجعل الفعل هو الذات، وهو به موصوف في الأزل والسؤال عن ذلك كالسؤال على أنه لم كان رباً عالما . ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And the affair of the Qadariyya is like that regarding what they are asked about the creation of acts, so they refer in the answer to the act of disbelief and sins. That is corrupt, because the way of this is sensory (sam'i), while the first (matter) which is described is rational. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: 'And the principle with us is that God Most High did not create any creation except that the effect of His grace upon it is apparent, and the proofs of His generosity in it are clear, and that His wisdom, through what is in it of evidence of His oneness, exists, and the proof and execution of His will in it are verified, and the sign of His power and knowledge of the realities of things is not hidden in that. And the question: "Why did You not bestow grace?" or "Why did You show Your generosity?" and "Why was wisdom?" and "Why did You establish the proof of Your oneness?" up to what was mentioned is absurd and corrupt, unacceptable to reason and not within its capacity due to its ugliness. Therefore, this type of question is invalid. And with God is success. His authority. Then it is permissible to say: since He is generous by His essence, and powerful by His essence, and knowing by His essence, He was generous with His creation upon His creation; since He is His creation, and He is able to be generous and show His gifts. And the basis of this question with us is corrupt, because we make the act be the essence, and He is described by it in pre-eternity, and the question about that is like the question about why He was Lord, knowing. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya sect. The author begins by describing their flawed methodology: when asked about the creation of actions, they resort to citing acts of disbelief and sin in their answer. This is invalid because the basis of that answer is sensory (sam'i) while the original issue (creation of acts) is rational. Then he states the principle: God's creation always manifests His grace, generosity, wisdom, proof of oneness, power, and knowledge. Therefore, questions like 'why did You not bestow grace?' or 'why did You show Your generosity?' are absurd and rejected by reason. He then adds a further argument: it is permissible to say that since God is generous, powerful, and knowing by His essence, He acted generously through His creation. The basis of such questioning is invalid because we consider the act to be identical with the essence (i.e., not separate from His attributes), and questioning that is like questioning why He is Lord and Knowing.

Key Terms
القدرية
خلق الأفعال
سمعي
عقلي
نعمه
جوده
حكمته
حجة وحدانيته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that questioning God's actions is valid if based on scripture.
Correction: This passage shows that even scripture-based questions are invalid when the issue is rational, because the answer would be mismatched.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Maturidi, why is the Qadariyya's answer (referring to acts of disbelief) invalid?
A) Because it relies on revelation while the question is rational.
B) Because it relies on reason while the question is revelatory.
C) Because it uses both reason and revelation.
D) Because it is forbidden to talk about such matters.

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya's error lies in using a transmitted answer for a rational question, and God's creation always manifests His perfect attributes, rendering such questioning invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself inwardly questioning why God allowed a specific trial in your life, while ignoring the clear signs of His grace and wisdom that are already manifest? What would it take for you to replace that question with gratitude and trust?
?
When you witness injustice or suffering in the world, does your heart ever accuse God of not being good or powerful enough? How can the principle that every creation shows proof of His will and knowledge reshape that reaction into a recognition of His perfect attributes?
?
Which of the divine attributes mentioned in this passage—grace, generosity, wisdom, power, or knowledge—do you most need to affirm today in the face of a situation that tempts you to question God's decree? Commit to repeating that attribute as a dhikr.

God's Acts and Attributes: The Identity Principle
Imam Maturidi argues that God's acts are from His essential attributes and questioning them is invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Maturidi's argument that God's acts are not separate from His essence, and therefore questioning them is as absurd as questioning His divinity and knowledge.

Core Idea
God's acts are identical with His essence; questioning them is like asking why He is Lord.

After establishing that creation manifests divine attributes, Imam Maturidi presents a further argument: since God is generous, powerful, and knowing by His essence, His act of creation is a necessary expression of those essential attributes. Thus, questioning it is akin to questioning why He is the Lord or why He knows.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the flow of the argument: it starts with a premise about God's essential attributes.
Focus on the phrases 'جواد بذاته', 'قادر بذاته', 'عالم بذاته'.
2
Understand the concept of essential attributes
God is generous by His essence, not by an attribute separate from Him. Therefore, His act of creation is a necessary consequence.
This is a key Maturidi doctrine.
3
Analyze the analogy
The passage compares questioning the act of creation to questioning why God is Lord or knowing. Understand why this analogy shows the invalidity of such questions.
Both are rooted in the essence and thus beyond 'why'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى ذلك شأن القدرية فيما يُسألون عن خلق الأفعال، فيرجعون في الجواب إلى فعل الكفر والمعاصي. وذلك فاسد، لأن طريق هذا سمعي، والأول الذي وصف عقلي. قال الشيخ رحمه الله : والأصل عندنا أن الله تعالى لم يخلق خلقا إلا وأثر نعمه عليه ظاهر، وأدلة جوده فيه بين، وأن حكمته بما فيه من دلالة وحدانيته موجودة، وبرهان ونفاذ مشيئته فيه محقق، وعلامة قدرته وعلمه بحقائق الأشياء غير خفى في ذلك. والسؤال على أنك لم أنعمت أو لماذا أظهرت جودك، ولم كانت الحكمة، ولم أقمت حجة وحدانيتك ؟ إلى آخر ما ذكر محال فاسد لا يقبله عقل ولا يحتمله وسع لقبحه . لذلك بطل هذا النوع من السؤال. وبالله التوفيق. سلطانه ثم جائز أن يقال: إذ هو بذاته جواد، وبذاته قادر، وبذاته عالم فجاد بخلقه على خلقه؛ إذ هو خلقه، إذ هو قادر على أن يجود ويُظهر مواهبه. وأصل هذا السؤال عندنا فاسد، لأنا نجعل الفعل هو الذات، وهو به موصوف في الأزل والسؤال عن ذلك كالسؤال على أنه لم كان رباً عالما . ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And the affair of the Qadariyya is like that regarding what they are asked about the creation of acts, so they refer in the answer to the act of disbelief and sins. That is corrupt, because the way of this is sensory (sam'i), while the first (matter) which is described is rational. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: 'And the principle with us is that God Most High did not create any creation except that the effect of His grace upon it is apparent, and the proofs of His generosity in it are clear, and that His wisdom, through what is in it of evidence of His oneness, exists, and the proof and execution of His will in it are verified, and the sign of His power and knowledge of the realities of things is not hidden in that. And the question: "Why did You not bestow grace?" or "Why did You show Your generosity?" and "Why was wisdom?" and "Why did You establish the proof of Your oneness?" up to what was mentioned is absurd and corrupt, unacceptable to reason and not within its capacity due to its ugliness. Therefore, this type of question is invalid. And with God is success. His authority. Then it is permissible to say: since He is generous by His essence, and powerful by His essence, and knowing by His essence, He was generous with His creation upon His creation; since He is His creation, and He is able to be generous and show His gifts. And the basis of this question with us is corrupt, because we make the act be the essence, and He is described by it in pre-eternity, and the question about that is like the question about why He was Lord, knowing. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya sect. The author begins by describing their flawed methodology: when asked about the creation of actions, they resort to citing acts of disbelief and sin in their answer. This is invalid because the basis of that answer is sensory (sam'i) while the original issue (creation of acts) is rational. Then he states the principle: God's creation always manifests His grace, generosity, wisdom, proof of oneness, power, and knowledge. Therefore, questions like 'why did You not bestow grace?' or 'why did You show Your generosity?' are absurd and rejected by reason. ?

?

?
You have just learned that questioning God's act is like questioning why He is Lord. The next time you catch yourself complaining about your provision, your health, or your circumstances, what concrete step will you take to remind yourself that His act is His essence, and that your complaint is a problem in your own heart?

Turning the Astrologers' Analogy Against Them
Al-Maturidi refutes astrologers using their own analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Maturidi uses the astrologers' own claim about the Maker's perfect action to argue for a wise manager of the stars.

Core Idea
The Maker's perfect action implies the stars are managed by a wise being.

Al-Maturidi begins by engaging with the astrologers' argument, which they share with natural philosophers. They claim the Maker's action is perfect because of His knowledge and power. Al-Maturidi turns this against them: if that is so, the stars must similarly be under the management of a wise, knowing creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening analogy
Read the Arabic and translation of the first part. Notice how Al-Maturidi presents the astrologers' argument before refuting it.
The astrologers compare the Maker's action to the natural philosophers' idea of nature.
2
Identify the key claim
The astrologers say the Maker's action is perfect due to knowledge and power. Al-Maturidi then says 'so the matter of the stars is similar.'
He is using their own logic to lead to a different conclusion.
3
Understand the redirection
Ask: What does the similarity imply? Al-Maturidi argues that if the Maker's perfect action required knowledge and power, then the stars' order must also come from a wise, knowing manager.
This sets up the need for a single wise manager, not multiple celestial agents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تكلم هؤلاء بما تكلم به أصحاب الطبائع : إن ذلك الصانع إنما خرج فعله محكما متقنا بما عنده من العلم وله من القدرة، ولولا ذلك لما احتمل ما ذكرت؛ فإنه بما سبق من التدبير استقام ذلك؛ فمثله أمر النجوم . لو كان على ما يقول / كان يكون ذلك كذلك يتدبير عليم حكيم أنشأها على ذلك. ولو كان إليها التدبير لما يحتمل أن تُتعب نفسها بالسير والحركات الدائمة وتؤلمها؛ إذ كذلك حال الأحياء في الشاهد: إن تلك الأحوال تتعبهم وتؤلمهم أو أن يكون من الموات فيكون بتدبير غيرها كان الذي [كان "]، على ما ذكر من قصة الديباج. على أنه يُعلم أنه لو قدر على ذلك بلا إتعاب نفسه لاختاره عليه. لِيُعْلَمْ أن كل ذلك بتدبير حكيم عليم غنى استعمل جميع ما ذكر فيما ذكر . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وبعد، فإنه لو جاز القول في عالمنا : إنه بتدبير من ذكر الجاز مثله فيمن ذكر أنه كان بتدبير من يعلوه، كذلك إلى ما لا نهاية له، وفي ذلك بطلان قولهم في تدبير النجوم؛ أو يرجع نهاية، وفي ذلك فساد قولهم في رفع النهاية عن الأشياء وإيجاب القول بواحد [إليه ] يرجع تدبير جميع ما ذكر ، وهو العالم بعواقب الأمور المقدر في كل ما إليه ينتهي. على أن هؤلاء قد أقروا بقولهم أن ليس لهم قول، لأنهم زعموا أن لا اختيار لهم، لكنهم مضطرون فيما يقولون، وكذلك خصومهم فيما يكذبونهم فيكون ذلك التكاذب والتناقض من هذا المدبر، ومن ذلك تدبيره فهو المفسد، ومن ذلك قدر قوله فهو لم يقل عند نفسه. وفي ذلك وجهان؛ أحدهما سقوط قوله فيبقى قول الموحدين والثاني إنكاره العيان والاختيار الذي يعلمه كل أحد وكل عاقل. ومن أنكر العيان [الذي ] يحيط به حسته، ثم يدعى غائبا ـ لا يبلغه حسته ـ بالذي أنكر مما أدركه حسته فهو بحمد الله / مكفى المؤونة وحقيق الهجر. وبالله المعونة.
Then these people spoke as the natural philosophers spoke: That the Maker (الصانع) brought forth His action perfectly and precisely due to the knowledge He possesses and the power He has, and were it not for that, what you mentioned would not be possible; for it was through preceding management that it became sound; so the matter of the stars is similar. If it were as they say, it would be by the management of a wise knowing one who established them accordingly. And if the management belonged to them, it would not be possible that they would fatigue themselves with constant motion and movement and cause them pain; for such is the case of living beings in the witnessed world: these states tire and pain them. Or if they are inanimate, then they are under the management of another; it would be as mentioned in the story of the brocade. Moreover, it is known that if He had the power to do so without fatiguing Himself, He would choose that. So that it be known that all of that is by the management of a wise, knowing, self-sufficient Being who used all that has been mentioned for what was mentioned. And there is no power except with Allah. And further, if it were permissible to say about our world that it is managed by whom was mentioned, then it would be permissible likewise concerning that manager that he was managed by one above him, and so on ad infinitum, and in that is the invalidation of their claim about the management of the stars; or it must end at a limit, and in that is the corruption of their claim of removing limits from things and the necessity of affirming a single One to Whom the management of all that has been mentioned returns, and He is the Knower of the outcomes of affairs, the Determiner in everything that ends with Him. Moreover, these people have admitted in their statement that they have no statement, because they claimed that they have no choice, but they are compelled in what they say, and likewise their opponents in what they deny them, so that mutual denial and contradiction is from this Manager, and from that management He is the corruptor, and from that measure of His speech, He has not spoken from Himself. In that are two aspects: one is the falling away of their statement, so the statement of the monotheists remains; the second is their denial of the observation and choice that everyone and every rational person knows. And whoever denies the observation that his sense encompasses, then claims an absent thing that his sense does not reach, with that which he denied from what his sense perceived, then, by the praise of Allah, he has been relieved of burden and is deserving of abandonment. And with Allah is assistance.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a multi-layered refutation of the astrologers' position. First, Al-Maturidi presents their own argument: the Maker's action is perfect due to His knowledge and power, and the stars' movements are similarly managed. He then turns this argument against them: if the stars managed the world, they would suffer pain and fatigue from constant motion—just as living beings do. If the stars are inanimate, then they are managed by another, leading to an infinite regress or a final Manager. Second, he argues that if the world's management is traced back, it must end with a single wise, knowing, self-sufficient Being, not multiple celestial agents. Third, he highlights a self-contradiction in the astrologers' deterministic claim: they say they have no choice, yet they are arguing and opposing others. Their own denial of choice invalidates their speech and leads to absurd consequences: either their statement falls away (monotheism remains), or they deny the manifest fact of choice and observation. Finally, he condemns those who deny clear sense perception (العيان) while claiming unseen things; such people are refuted by their own senses. This conclusively establishes the necessity of a single wise Creator and the invalidity of astrological determinism.

Key Terms
صانع
تدبير
علم
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The stars independently manage the world's affairs.
Correction: Al-Maturidi shows that if the Maker's action requires knowledge and power, the stars' order also requires a wise manager, not themselves.

Checkpoint
What does Al-Maturidi compare the matter of the stars to?
A) The Maker's perfect action due to knowledge and power
B) The natural philosophers' view of nature
C) An independent deterministic system
D) The story of the brocade

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi uses the astrologers' own premise—that the Maker's action is perfect due to knowledge and power—to argue that the stars must be managed by a wise being.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever attribute the order in your life to luck or your own planning, forgetting that it is ultimately under the management of a Wise Being? How can you remind yourself daily that every small detail is under His tadbīr?
?
When you look at the stars tonight, will you see them as mere celestial bodies or as signs pointing to their Creator? What practical difference would that make in your worship and reliance on God?
?
Al-Maturidi uses his opponent's logic against them. Is there an argument you have accepted from the world that actually, if followed through, leads back to God? Will you trace it to its conclusion and let it strengthen your faith?

Pain, Fatigue, and the Need for a Single Manager
Al-Maturidi argues stars cannot self-manage and infinite regress requires a single manager.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Maturidi's arguments that stars cannot manage themselves due to pain/fatigue and that infinite regress forces a single final manager.

Core Idea
If stars managed the world, they would suffer endless pain; only a single wise manager avoids absurdity.

Al-Maturidi now pushes the astrologers' claim to its logical consequences. He considers two possibilities: if stars are living beings, their constant motion would cause them pain; if inanimate, they must be managed by another. This leads to an infinite regress that can only be resolved by affirming a single, wise, self-sufficient manager. The argument is powerful and definitive.

Guided Path
1
Read the pain/fatigue argument
Read the Arabic and translation starting from 'ولو كان إليها التدبير' to 'على ما ذكر من قصة الديباج'. Notice the two cases: living vs. inanimate stars.
The 'story of the brocade' is a known analogy for something having a maker.
2
Trace the infinite regress
Read from 'وبعد، فإنه لو جاز القول' to 'المقدر في كل ما إليه ينتهي'. See how Al-Maturidi shows that if each manager has a manager above, it goes on forever, which invalidates their claim, or it ends at a single manager.
This is a classic argument for a first cause.
3
Identify the conclusion
The conclusion is that all management returns to one wise, knowing being who determines all outcomes. This is the monotheistic position.
Al-Maturidi uses the astrologers' own framework to prove the necessity of a single creator.

Source Text

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Multiple celestial agents can independently manage the world without a final authority.
Correction: Al-Maturidi shows that such an assumption leads to infinite regress or absurd pain for the stars; only a single wise manager resolves the issue.

Checkpoint
What is one consequence of allowing an infinite chain of managers?
A) The claim about stars' management is strengthened
B) The claim about stars' management is invalidated
C) The stars become self-sufficient
D) The final manager becomes unnecessary

Key Takeaway
The argument from infinite regress forces the conclusion that there must be a single, wise, self-sufficient manager for all celestial and earthly affairs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever relied on horoscopes, lucky charms, or other superstitions to decide your actions? How does this logical argument challenge the very foundation of such beliefs? Will you still give them any weight in your life?
?
The argument shows that an infinite chain of managers is absurd. In your own life, are there areas where you keep making excuses or shifting responsibility instead of accepting a single ultimate accountability before Allah? How can you stop that regress today?
?
If you truly internalized that a single wise Being manages every detail of the universe—including your pain and fatigue—how would that change your response to hardship? Can you trust Him even when you don't see the purpose?

The Self-Contradiction of Determinism and Affirmation of Choice
Al-Maturidi exposes the self-contradiction in the astrologers' determinism and affirms choice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Maturidi exposes the self-contradiction in the astrologers' deterministic claim and affirms the evident reality of choice and observation.

Core Idea
Determinism is self-refuting: if you have no choice, your argument is not yours.

In this final part, Al-Maturidi delivers a devastating logical blow. The astrologers claim they have no choice in what they say—they are compelled. Al-Maturidi points out that this very claim is self-contradictory: if they have no choice, their statements are not their own, and their opposition to opponents is also from the same manager. He then presents two devastating consequences, and concludes that denying the manifest observation of choice is absurd.

Guided Path
1
Read the admission of determinism
Read from 'على أن هؤلاء قد أقروا' to 'فهو لم يقل عند نفسه'. Note that the astrologers admit they have no choice.
They say they are compelled (مضطرون) in what they say.
2
Understand the self-contradiction
If they have no choice, their own speech is not freely chosen. Their denial of their opponents' statements is also compelled. This leads to the whole dispute being from the same manager, which is absurd.
This is a classic refutation of determinism known as 'the argument from self-refutation'.
3
Learn the two aspects
Al-Maturidi gives two possibilities: (1) their statement falls away, leaving monotheism; (2) they deny the evident choice and observation, which is irrational.
Both options defeat their position.
4
Reflect on the denial of observation
Al-Maturidi says whoever denies what his senses perceive (like choice) while claiming unseen things is refuted by his own senses. Such a person is worthy of abandonment.
This affirms the empirical reality of human choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تكلم هؤلاء بما تكلم به أصحاب الطبائع : إن ذلك الصانع إنما خرج فعله محكما متقنا بما عنده من العلم وله من القدرة، ولولا ذلك لما احتمل ما ذكرت؛ فإنه بما سبق من التدبير استقام ذلك؛ فمثله أمر النجوم . لو كان على ما يقول / كان يكون ذلك كذلك يتدبير عليم حكيم أنشأها على ذلك. ولو كان إليها التدبير لما يحتمل أن تُتعب نفسها بالسير والحركات الدائمة وتؤلمها؛ إذ كذلك حال الأحياء في الشاهد: إن تلك الأحوال تتعبهم وتؤلمهم أو أن يكون من الموات فيكون بتدبير غيرها كان الذي [كان "]، على ما ذكر من قصة الديباج. على أنه يُعلم أنه لو قدر على ذلك بلا إتعاب نفسه لاختاره عليه. لِيُعْلَمْ أن كل ذلك بتدبير حكيم عليم غنى استعمل جميع ما ذكر فيما ذكر . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وبعد، فإنه لو جاز القول في عالمنا : إنه بتدبير من ذكر الجاز مثله فيمن ذكر أنه كان بتدبير من يعلوه، كذلك إلى ما لا نهاية له، وفي ذلك بطلان قولهم في تدبير النجوم؛ أو يرجع نهاية، وفي ذلك فساد قولهم في رفع النهاية عن الأشياء وإيجاب القول بواحد [إليه ] يرجع تدبير جميع ما ذكر ، وهو العالم بعواقب الأمور المقدر في كل ما إليه ينتهي. على أن هؤلاء قد أقروا بقولهم أن ليس لهم قول، لأنهم زعموا أن لا اختيار لهم، لكنهم مضطرون فيما يقولون، وكذلك خصومهم فيما يكذبونهم فيكون ذلك التكاذب والتناقض من هذا المدبر، ومن ذلك تدبيره فهو المفسد، ومن ذلك قدر قوله فهو لم يقل عند نفسه. وفي ذلك وجهان؛ أحدهما سقوط قوله فيبقى قول الموحدين والثاني إنكاره العيان والاختيار الذي يعلمه كل أحد وكل عاقل. ومن أنكر العيان [الذي ] يحيط به حسته، ثم يدعى غائبا ـ لا يبلغه حسته ـ بالذي أنكر مما أدركه حسته فهو بحمد الله / مكفى المؤونة وحقيق الهجر. وبالله المعونة.
Then these people spoke as the natural philosophers spoke: That the Maker (الصانع) brought forth His action perfectly and precisely due to the knowledge He possesses and the power He has, and were it not for that, what you mentioned would not be possible; for it was through preceding management that it became sound; so the matter of the stars is similar. If it were as they say, it would be by the management of a wise knowing one who established them accordingly. And if the management belonged to them, it would not be possible that they would fatigue themselves with constant motion and movement and cause them pain; for such is the case of living beings in the witnessed world: these states tire and pain them. Or if they are inanimate, then they are under the management of another; it would be as mentioned in the story of the brocade. Moreover, it is known that if He had the power to do so without fatiguing Himself, He would choose that. So that it be known that all of that is by the management of a wise, knowing, self-sufficient Being who used all that has been mentioned for what was mentioned. And there is no power except with Allah. And further, if it were permissible to say about our world that it is managed by whom was mentioned, then it would be permissible likewise concerning that manager that he was managed by one above him, and so on ad infinitum, and in that is the invalidation of their claim about the management of the stars; or it must end at a limit, and in that is the corruption of their claim of removing limits from things and the necessity of affirming a single One to Whom the management of all that has been mentioned returns, and He is the Knower of the outcomes of affairs, the Determiner in everything that ends with Him. Moreover, these people have admitted in their statement that they have no statement, because they claimed that they have no choice, but they are compelled in what they say, and likewise their opponents in what they deny them, so that mutual denial and contradiction is from this Manager, and from that management He is the corruptor, and from that measure of His speech, He has not spoken from Himself. In that are two aspects: one is the falling away of their statement, so the statement of the monotheists remains; the second is their denial of the observation and choice that everyone and every rational person knows. And whoever denies the observation that his sense encompasses, then claims an absent thing that his sense does not reach, with that which he denied from what his sense perceived, then, by the praise of Allah, he has been relieved of burden and is deserving of abandonment. And with Allah is assistance.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a multi-layered refutation of the astrologers' position. First, Al-Maturidi presents their own argument: the Maker's action is perfect due to His knowledge and power, and the stars' movements are similarly managed. He then turns this argument against them: if the stars managed the world, they would suffer pain and fatigue from constant motion—just as living beings do. If the stars are inanimate, then they are managed by another, leading to an infinite regress or a final Manager. Second, he argues that if the world's management is traced back, it must end with a single wise, knowing, self-sufficient Being, not multiple celestial agents. Third, he highlights a self-contradiction in the astrologers' deterministic claim: they say they have no choice, yet they are arguing and opposing others. Their own denial of choice invalidates their speech and leads to absurd consequences: either their statement falls away (monotheism remains), or they deny the manifest fact of choice and observation. Finally, he condemns those who deny clear sense perception (العيان) while claiming unseen things; such people are refuted by their own senses. This conclusively establishes the necessity of a single wise Creator and the invalidity of astrological determinism.

Key Terms
اختيار
جبر
عيان
تكاذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying free choice is a humble and consistent position.
Correction: Al-Maturidi shows it is self-contradictory and denies the obvious reality of choice experienced by every rational person.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Maturidi, what is one of the two aspects of the astrologers' admission of no choice?
A) Their statement becomes more credible
B) Their statement falls away and the monotheists' statement remains
C) They are forced to become astrologers
D) Their admission is accepted without consequence

Key Takeaway
The deterministic claim is self-refuting because it denies the very choice required to make a meaningful argument; the evident reality of human choice is affirmed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make excuses for your sins by saying 'it was written for me,' are you not denying the very choice Allah has made evident in your heart? What will you do tomorrow to own your actions instead of hiding behind fate?
?
This passage exposes the contradiction in arguing passionately for a belief while living as though your choices don't matter. Where in your life do you see this disconnect? How can you align your speech and your actions starting today?
?
Al-Maturidi says that denying the clear observation of choice is irrational. In what area of your life are you currently denying what you know to be true about your own responsibility? What step will you take today to act on that truth?

The Foundation of the Trial: Discrimination
Maturidi praises God and introduces creation for trial with discrimination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God created humans for a trial and granted them the ability to discriminate between good and bad, establishing the basis for moral responsibility.

Core Idea
Humans are created for a trial through the gift of discrimination.

Maturidi opens the discussion on human actions by praising God's unique attributes and immediately ties creation to a divine test. He explains that God equipped humans with the faculty of discrimination (tamyiz) and knowledge of what is praiseworthy and blameworthy. This passage lays the groundwork for understanding human moral agency as a deliberate part of God's wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening praise
Notice how Maturidi begins with God's attributes of pre-eternity and power, setting a reverent tone. This establishes the authority of the Creator who designs the test.
2
Identify the purpose of creation
After the transition 'أما بعد', Maturidi states that God created humans 'for trial' (للمحنة). This is the core purpose. Underline this phrase.
3
Understand discrimination and knowledge
God made humans 'people of discrimination and knowledge' (أهل تمييز وعلم). This means they can distinguish between good and bad. The passage specifies that God made bad things appear 'ugly' (قبيحا) in their minds and good things 'beautiful' (حسنًا).
This is the foundation of moral evaluation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في أفعال الخلق وإثباتها
الحمد لله المتوحد بالقدم والإلهية، المتفرد بالدوام والربوبية، ذي البرهان المنير والملك الكبير؛ الذي فطر الخلق بقدرته، وصرفهم بحكمته على سابق علمه ومشيئته، وتقلب كل بريته في مواهبه وإحسانه. أنشأ الأشياء كيف شاء، لا يسأل عما يفعل وهم يسألون [الأنبياء، ۲۳/۲۱]، لما يتمكن منهم السفه والحكمة، ليزجروا بالسؤال ثم بالجزاء عن ويرغبوا في الحكمة. ونسأله أن يكرمنا بالتوفيق، ويجدر عزمنا التسديد، وينور قلوبنا بالتوحيد، فإنه حميد مجيد. أما بعد، فإن الله تعالى لما خلق البشر للمحنة بما جعلهم أهل تمييز وعلم بالمحمود من الأمور والمذموم، وجعل ما يذم منها قبيحا في عقولهم، وما يُحمد حسنًا، وعظم في أذهانهم إيثار القبيح على الحسن والرغبة فيما يُذم على ما يُحمد، دعاهم - على ما عليه ركبوا وما به أكرموا - إلى إيثار أمر على أمر، وقبح في عقولهم احتمال أمثالهم [غيره]. جعل الله جميع ما لهم فيه متقلب بين ضرر يتقى ونفع يُرغب فيه، ليكون ذلك لهم علمًا للموعود مما به الترغيب والترهيب وأنشأهم على طبائع تنفر عن أشياء وتميل إلى أشياء، وأراهم في عقولهم حُسن بعض ما تنفر عنه الطباع بحمد العواقب، وقبح بعض ما تميل إليه بذم العواقب فصيرهم بحيث يحتملون المكروه على الطباع بلذيذ العاقبة، ويقهرونه عما يدعوهم إليه بشهى النهاية. ثم امتحنهم إذ أبت عقولهم احتمال أمثالها، ورغب في محاسن الأعمال ومكارم الأخلاق باختيار ما حسن من الأعمال واجتناب ما قبح من ذلك. ثم جعل ما فيه محنهم أمرين: العسير
A question on the actions of creatures and their affirmation. Praise be to God, the Unique in pre-eternity and divinity, the Singular in perpetuity and lordship, the Possessor of clear proof and great dominion; who created creatures by His power, and directed them by His wisdom according to His prior knowledge and will, and the turning of all His creation in His gifts and beneficence. He originated things as He willed; He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned [Quran 21:23], because foolishness and wisdom are possible for them, so that they may be deterred by questioning and then by recompense from [evil] and desire wisdom. And we ask Him to honor us with success, to renew our resolution for right guidance, and to illuminate our hearts with tawhid, for He is Praiseworthy, Glorious. To proceed: God Almighty, when He created humans for trial, made them people of discrimination and knowledge of what is praiseworthy and blameworthy among matters, and He made what is blameworthy ugly in their minds, and what is praiseworthy beautiful, and He magnified in their minds the preference of the ugly over the beautiful and the desire for what is blameworthy over what is praiseworthy. He called them—upon the nature on which they were created and with which they were honored—to prefer one matter over another, and He made in their minds the likelihood of their peers [others] ugly. God made all that they have in which they turn between harm to be avoided and benefit to be desired, so that this would be for them a sign of what is promised regarding encouragement and discouragement. And He created them with natures that shrink from some things and incline to others, and He showed in their minds the beauty of some of what nature shrinks from due to praise of outcomes, and the ugliness of some of what it inclines to due to blame of outcomes. Thus He made them such that they bear the disliked in nature for the pleasure of the outcome, and overcome it from what calls them through the desire of the end. Then He tested them when their minds refused the likelihood of their peers, and they desired the good deeds and noble morals by choosing what is good of deeds and avoiding what is ugly of that. Then He made what is in their trial two things: the difficult
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on human actions and their affirmation. Maturidi starts with praise of God's attributes of pre-eternity, divinity, etc., and then cites the Quranic verse about not being questioned, noting that humans are capable of both foolishness and wisdom, so questioning serves to deter and guide them. He then invokes divine assistance. The core discussion begins: God created humans for trial (mihna) by giving them the ability to discriminate (tamyiz) and knowledge of good and bad. He made the bad appear ugly in their minds and the good beautiful, but also magnified in their minds the inclination to prefer the ugly over the beautiful—a test of their choice. God then set up their existence as a constant fluctuation between harm to be avoided and benefit to be desired, serving as signs of divine promises. He created them with natural dispositions that repel some things and incline to others, but through reason they can see the positive outcomes of repulsive actions and the negative outcomes of attractive ones, so they bear temporary hardship for long-term benefit. Next, when their minds refused to accept the likelihood of their peers (i.e., they were unique in responsibility?), they desired good actions and noble character by choice. Finally, the test is summarized as two matters: the difficult (and presumably the easy, but the text breaks off).

الخلق
المحنة
التمييز
الحسن
القبيح

According to this passage, what did God create humans for?
A) Mere enjoyment
B) Trial (mihna)
C) Worship only
D) Random existence

Key Takeaway
Humans are deliberately created for a trial, and God gave them discrimination and an innate sense of good and bad as the foundation of that test.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a decision between right and wrong, do you trust that innate sense of ugliness and beauty that God placed in your heart, or do you override it with desires? What would it take for you to obey that inner compass completely?
?
If God created you specifically for this trial, how are you treating the test? Are you actively using your discrimination to seek what is praiseworthy, or are you numbing that sense through neglect? Write down one specific area where you have ignored the ugliness of a blameworthy action.
?
The passage says God made blameworthy actions 'ugly in their minds.' Think of a sin you have committed recently: did you not feel a natural repulsion before you did it? Why did you proceed? Repent and resolve to listen to that God-given warning next time.

The Mechanics of the Test: Nature and Reason
Maturidi explains the divine test through nature, reason, and choice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God tests humans by creating conflicting natural inclinations and using reason to guide them toward beneficial outcomes, forming the essence of moral choice.

Core Idea
God tests humans by pitting their natural desires against rational outcomes.

Having established that humans are endowed with discrimination, Maturidi now reveals the intricate dynamics of the test. He explains that God magnified the appeal of the ugly in human minds, created natural dispositions that repel or attract, and then showed reason the true consequences of actions. This passage demonstrates how humans are called to bear temporary hardship for eternal reward.

Guided Path
1
Observe the magnification of preference
Maturidi says God intensified the desire for the ugly over the beautiful. This is part of the test—humans must overcome this inclination.
2
Trace the role of nature and reason
God created natures (tabai') that shrink from some things and incline to others. Then He shows in their minds the beauty of outcomes from repulsive actions and the ugliness of outcomes from attractive actions.
Reason sees beyond immediate inclination.
3
Recognize the call to choose
God calls humans to prefer one thing over another, and they can bear the disliked for a pleasant outcome. This is the test of patience and wisdom.
4
Identify the final test
When minds refused to accept the likelihood of peers (i.e., uniqueness of responsibility), they desired good deeds by choice. The trial is summarized as two matters: the difficult (and the easy, though the text breaks off).

Key Takeaway
The divine test involves overcoming natural inclinations through reason, focusing on ultimate outcomes, and making conscious choices toward good deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What is one area of your life where your natural inclinations pull you toward something that you know has a blameworthy outcome? Are you willing to bear the temporary discomfort because you trust God's promise of a better reward?
?
The passage teaches that God showed us the beauty of outcomes that initially seem unpleasant. Think of a noble deed you find hard to do. How does focusing on its ultimate benefit (pleasing Allah, eternal reward) change your motivation to do it?
?
When you realize that you are personally responsible for your choices (not your peers), does that make you more eager to choose good deeds? How can you use that sense of accountability to overcome laziness or peer pressure today?

The First Argument: Acts Must Be Attributed to God as True Agent
First argument: acts must be attributed to God as true agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first argument that all acts must be attributed to God because He is the sole true agent and nothing escapes His power.

Core Idea
Acts are real for God, metaphorical for humans, because God is the only true agent.

This lesson presents the first of three arguments used by those who claim human acts are only metaphorical. It focuses on divine agency: since God is the truly powerful and incapable of being incapacitated, acts cannot be genuinely attributed to anyone else. Human language may assign acts to creatures, but that is merely figurative.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the first argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the argument begins with the obligation of attributing acts to God.
2
Identify the key premises
Identify the premises: God is the true agent (الفاعل الحق) and nothing escapes His power. Then note that many things clearly from God are linguistically attributed to humans.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Reflect on the conclusion that even if all acts are linguistically attributed to humans, they remain metaphorical in reality. Why does the argument insist on real attribution to God?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله : } اختلف منتحلوا الإسلام في أفعال الخلق. فمنهم من جعلها لهم مجازاً، وحقيقتها الله بأوجه أحدها وجوب إضافتها إلى الله على ما أضيف إليه خلق كل شيء في الجملة، فلم يجز أن يكون الإضافة إلى الله مجازاً، لأنه الفاعل الحق والقادر الذي لا يعجزه شيء؛ وفي ذلك إخراج عن قدرته وإزالة عن حقيقة فعله. وقد أضيف كثير مما لا يُشك على أن الله هو منشؤه إلى العباد بالحرف الذي هو حرف العبارة عن الأفعال كالموت والحياة، والطول والقصر، والحركة والسكون، والاجتماع والتفرق. والله سبحانه لكل ذلك فاعل وعلى كله قادر فمثله ما ذكرنا. وإضافة ذلك في القرآن ظاهر وذهب هؤلاء في التعذيب ونحو ذلك إلى أن له الخلق والأمر بكليته، له في ذلك ما شاء، على ما قدر لكل مالك في ملكه ما له فيه، وإن كان ذلك كله على هذا القول مجازياً. والثاني أن بتحقيق الفعل لغيره تشابها في الفعل، وقد نفي الله ذلك بقوله : أم جعلوا الله شركاء خلقوا كخلقه فتشابه الخلق عليهم. وإذا لم يكن حقيقة الإملاك في الجواهر وفي الإلزام يقع تشابه في الملك، فمثله في الأفعال. والثالث أيضا إنه لو جعل للعبد إيجاد وإخراج من العدم لكان في معنى «خلق»، فيلزم اسم «خالق»، وذلك مما أباه الجميع، حيث قالوا: لا خالق إلا الله. قال الشيخ رحمه الله : } وعندنا لازم تحقيق الفعل لهم بالسمع والعقل والضرورة التي
The jurist, may God have mercy on him, said: 'The claimants to Islam differed regarding the acts of creatures. Among them are those who made them metaphorical for them, and their reality belongs to God, with aspects: first, the obligation of attributing them to God according to what the creation of everything is attributed to Him in general, so it is not permissible that attribution to God be metaphorical, because He is the true agent and the powerful who is not incapacitated by anything; and in that is removal from His power and removal from the reality of His act. And many things about which there is no doubt that God is their origin have been attributed to servants by the letter that is the letter of expression about acts, such as death and life, length and shortness, movement and stillness, gathering and separation. And God, glorified, is the agent of all that and powerful over all of it, and similar to what we mentioned. And the attribution of that in the Quran is apparent, and these people went, regarding punishment and the like, to the view that He has creation and command entirely, He has therein what He wills, according to what is decreed for every owner in his property of what he has therein, even if all that is metaphorical according to this saying. Second: that making the act real for another leads to similarity in act, and God negated that by His saying: 'Or have they associated partners with God who created like His creation so that the creation became similar to them?' And if the reality of ownership of substances and imposition does not imply similarity in ownership, then likewise in acts. Third: also that if the servant were given bringing into existence and bringing out from non-existence, it would be in the meaning of 'creation', and so the name 'creator' would necessarily follow, and that is what all reject, saying: There is no creator but God. The shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: 'And with us, the reality of the act for them is necessary by revelation, intellect, and necessity which...'
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a classification of views on human acts. Maturidi reports that among the claimants to Islam, one group makes acts metaphorical for humans and real for God, giving three reasons. First: Acts must be attributed to God because He is the true agent and nothing escapes His power. Many things that are clearly from God (like life, death, movement) are linguistically attributed to humans, but this is only metaphorical; the real agent is God. Second: If humans truly performed acts, there would be a similarity between Creator and creature, which God negated in the Quran (13:16). Just as ownership of substances does not imply similarity, so too with acts. Third: If humans could bring something from non-existence, they would be called 'khaliq' (creator), but all agree that there is no creator but God. Then Maturidi begins his own view: that acts are truly attributed to humans based on revelation, intellect, and necessity, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
أفعال الخلق
مجاز
حقيقة
خالق
إيجاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because we say 'I did this' in everyday language, our act is truly real and independent from God.
Correction: The argument insists that such language is metaphorical; the real agent is only God, as nothing escapes His power.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument, why is it not permissible for attribution to God to be metaphorical?
A) Because God is the true agent and nothing escapes His power
B) Because the Quran never uses metaphor
C) Because humans are not agents at all
D) Because the Prophet said so

Key Takeaway
The first argument holds that all acts must be truly attributed to God alone; human attribution is merely metaphorical language.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed in a task or achieve something good, to whom do you instinctively give credit? Does your heart truly attribute it entirely to God, or do you feel a sense of personal accomplishment? How can you train yourself to see God as the sole agent in every outcome?
?
This lesson says that even your faults and sins are ultimately from God's creation. How does that affect your view of your own failures? Do you blame yourself or despair, or do you turn to God as the only one who can change your state? What practical step can you take today to surrender your self-reliance?
?
If every act is metaphorical when attributed to you, what does that say about your prayers and worship? Are you merely the ‘location’ of an act that God brings about? How does this awareness transform your humility and your hope in God's mercy?

The Second Argument: Avoiding Similarity with God
Second argument: real human acts would imply similarity with God, negated in Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument that giving humans real agency would imply similarity between Creator and creature, which the Quran explicitly negates.

Core Idea
Real human agency would create resemblance to God, which the Quran denies.

The second argument draws from a Quranic verse that negates any similarity in creative power. If humans truly performed acts, they would be like creators, leading to a similarity that is rejected. The argument uses an analogy with ownership to clarify that real action does not entail similarity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the second argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the Quranic quotation and the ownership analogy.
2
Understand the Quranic basis
Identify the verse (Quran 13:16) that negates similarity in creation. Reflect on how this rejects real human agency.
3
Analyze the ownership analogy
The argument says that if ownership of substances and imposition does not imply similarity in ownership, then likewise acts do not imply similarity. Understand the logical parallel.

The Third Argument: No Creator but God
Third argument: human origination would imply 'creator' attribute, which is exclusive to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third argument that if humans could bring something from non-existence, they would be called 'creator', which is an exclusive attribute of God.

Core Idea
Bringing from non-existence is creation, and only God creates.

The third argument is straightforward and powerful: the term 'creator' (خالق) is reserved for God alone. If humans had the power to bring things from non-existence (إيجاد), they would be considered creators, which all Muslims unanimously reject. Therefore, human acts cannot be real in that sense.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the third argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the conditional statement: if humans could bring into existence, then 'creator' would apply.
2
Understand the term 'إيجاد'
Recognize that 'إيجاد' means bringing into existence from non-existence. This is the core of creation.
3
Reflect on the consensus
The argument ends by noting the universal agreement (الجميع) that 'There is no creator but God.' How does this support the view that human acts are metaphorical?

The First Argument: Attributing Actions to God Cannot Be Metaphorical
Maturidi presents the first reason why human actions cannot be merely metaphorical for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's first argument that attributing actions to God as merely metaphorical would deny His true agency and power.

Core Idea
If God's action attribution were metaphorical, His power would be denied.

Maturidi begins his refutation by establishing that since God is the true creator of everything, the attribution of actions to Him is literal, not metaphorical. He points out that even actions clearly from God—like death and life—are linguistically attributed to humans, showing the flaw in the metaphorical view.

Guided Path
1
Read the first argument passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Focus on Maturidi's main claim and the evidence he gives.
2
Identify the logical structure
Notice how Maturidi states that attributing actions to God cannot be metaphorical because He is the true agent and powerful. Then he gives linguistic examples.
The argument has two parts: a logical point and supporting examples.
3
Reflect on the implication
If the metaphorical view were true, it would imply that God is not truly the agent of actions. Why would that be problematic?
This connects to the core idea: it would remove God's power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله : اختلف منتحلوا الإسلام في أفعال الخلق. فمنهم من جعلها لهم مجازاً، وحقيقتها الله بأوجه أحدها وجوب إضافتها إلى الله على ما أضيف إليه خلق كل شيء في الجملة، فلم يجز أن يكون الإضافة إلى الله مجازاً، لأنه الفاعل الحق والقادر الذي لا يعجزه شيء؛ وفي ذلك إخراج عن قدرته وإزالة عن حقيقة فعله. وقد أضيف كثير مما لا يُشك على أن الله هو منشؤه إلى العباد بالحرف الذي هو حرف العبارة عن الأفعال كالموت والحياة، والطول والقصر، والحركة والسكون، والاجتماع والتفرق. والله سبحانه لكل ذلك فاعل وعلى كله قادر فمثله ما ذكرنا. وإضافة ذلك في القرآن ظاهر وذهب هؤلاء في التعذيب ونحو ذلك إلى أن له الخلق والأمر بكليته، له في ذلك ما شاء، على ما قدر لكل مالك في ملكه ما له فيه، وإن كان ذلك كله على هذا القول مجازياً. والثاني أن بتحقيق الفعل لغيره تشابها في الفعل، وقد نفي الله ذلك بقوله : أم جعلوا الله شركاء خلقوا كخلقه فتشابه الخلق عليهم . وإذا لم يكن حقيقة الإملاك في الجواهر وفي الإلزام يقع تشابه في الملك، فمثله في الأفعال و [الثالث] أيضا إنه لو جعل للعبد إيجاد وإخراج من العدم لكان في معنى / خلَق، فيلزم اسم «خالق»، وذلك مما أباه الجميع، حيث قالوا: لا خالق إلا الله .
The jurist (may God have mercy on him) said: The claimants of Islam differed concerning the actions of creatures. Among them are those who made them metaphorically for them, while their reality is for God, in aspects: one of them is the obligation of attributing them to God based on the attribution to Him of the creation of everything in general, so it is not permissible that the attribution to God be metaphorical, because He is the true agent and the powerful who is not incapacitated by anything; and in that is a removal from His power and a removal from the reality of His act. And much that is not doubted that God is its originator has been attributed to servants by the letter that is the letter of expression about actions, such as death and life, length and shortness, motion and rest, gathering and separation. And God the Exalted is the agent of all that and over all that is powerful, so the like of what we mentioned. And the attribution of that in the Qur'an is apparent, and these people went concerning punishment and the like to the view that to Him belongs creation and command entirely, for Him in that whatever He wills, according to what is decreed for every owner in his property of what is in it, even if all that according to this statement is metaphorical. And the second [aspect] is that the realization of the act for another causes similarity in the act, and God negated that with His statement: "Or have they made for God partners who created like His creation so that the creation became confused to them?" And if the reality of ownership in substances and in obligation does not occur, similarity in ownership occurs, so the like of it in actions. And [the third] also is that if making for the servant bringing into existence and bringing out from non-existence were [granted], it would be in the meaning of 'created', so the name 'creator' would be necessary, and that is what all abhorred, as they said: There is no creator but God.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that human actions are metaphorically attributed to humans while really belonging to God. Maturidi begins by noting that Muslims differed on human actions. Some held that actions are attributed to humans metaphorically, but in reality they are God's. He then gives three arguments against this view. The first argument: Since God is the true agent and creator of everything, it is impossible for His attribution of actions to be merely metaphorical. If it were metaphorical, it would imply that God is not truly the agent, which is false. Moreover, many things whose origin is clearly from God (like death, life, etc.) are linguistically attributed to humans in Arabic. The second argument: If humans truly created their actions, they would be like God in creating, which is negated by the Quranic verse 'Or have they made for God partners who created like His creation...' Since ownership cannot be truly shared, actions cannot be either. The third argument: If a servant could bring something from non-existence, he would be a creator, but Muslims agree that only God is creator. Therefore, the metaphorical view is false.

Key Terms
أفعال الخلق
مجاز
إضافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that since actions are linguistically attributed to humans, they are metaphorically theirs, while reality belongs to God.
Correction: Maturidi argues that linguistic attribution does not imply metaphor; the same language is used for actions clearly from God, proving that reality is literal for God.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Maturidi gives that attributing actions to God cannot be metaphorical?
A) Because humans have free will.
B) Because God is the true agent and powerful, so His actions are real.
C) Because the Qur'an uses metaphorical language.
D) Because actions are not real.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's first argument establishes that since God is the true agent, His attribution of actions cannot be metaphorical without denying His power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed in a task or overcome a difficulty, do you truly feel that God is the one who caused that success, or does your heart subtly attribute it to your own effort? How can you train yourself to see God's agency in every outcome?
?
If you believed with full certainty that every action—even your sins—is ultimately created by God, how would that transform your relationship with Him? Would it lead to more gratitude, humility, or something else? What holds you back from that belief?
?
The passage argues that attributing actions to God metaphorically would deny His power. In your daily life, where do you find yourself treating God's control as figurative rather than real? How can you make that belief literal and lived?

The Second Argument: True Action Would Imply Similarity to God
Maturidi presents the second argument against metaphorical attribution: it would imply similarity to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's second argument that if humans truly created their actions, they would be similar to God in creating, which the Qur'an denies.

Core Idea
If humans truly make actions, they would be like God—impossible.

Maturidi presents a second argument: if human actions were truly theirs (not metaphorical), they would be creators like God, leading to a false similarity. He cites the Qur'anic verse that negates the existence of partners who create like God's creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Read the passage starting from 'والثاني أن بتحقيق الفعل لغيره...' and its translation.
2
Understand the analogy with ownership
Maturidi draws an analogy: just as true ownership cannot be shared, true action (bringing from non-existence) cannot be shared without implying similarity to God.
The Qur'anic verse is key: 'Or have they made partners who created like His creation...'
3
Reflect on the implication
If any creature really performed an act of creation, they would be similar to God in that attribute. Why is that unacceptable?
This argument guards against associating partners with God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And much that is not doubted that God is its originator has been attributed to servants by the letter that is the letter of expression about actions, such as death and life, length and shortness, motion and rest, gathering and separation. The Third Argument: Human Creation Would Require the Title 'Creator'
Maturidi presents the third argument: human creation would demand the title 'creator', which Muslims reject.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's third argument: if humans could bring something from non-existence, they would be called 'creator', which Muslims unanimously deny.

Core Idea
If humans could create, they would be called 'creator'—but all Muslims deny that.

Maturidi's final argument is straightforward: if a servant could bring something from non-existence into existence, he would be similar to God in meaning, necessitating the title 'creator'. Since all Muslims agree that only God is creator, the metaphorical view is false.

Guided Path
1
Read the third argument
Read the Arabic and translation: 'والثالث أيضا إنه لو جعل للعبد إيجاد...'
2
Understand the logical implication
If a human can create from nothing, they are doing what only God does. That would imply the name 'creator' applies to them.
3
Note the consensus
Maturidi points out that all Muslims (الجميع) reject that anyone besides God is called 'creator'. This consensus is the final proof.
This shows the strength of the unbelief if one were to accept human creation.

Source Text

?
If the unanimous rejection of the title 'creator' for humans is so clear, why do you think your heart still sometimes seeks credit for what only God can do? What step will you take this week to redirect glory to Him when you receive praise?

Scriptural Evidence for Human Agency
Maturidi presents scriptural evidence for human agency and clarifies its compatibility with divine creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses scriptural commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats to prove that human actions are genuinely attributable to humans, without denying divine creation.

Core Idea
Scripture addresses humans as actors, proving their actions are truly theirs.

Maturidi begins by stating his position: human actions must be realized as truly theirs, based on three sources. In this lesson, we focus on the first source—revelation. He explains that God's commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats only make sense if humans genuinely perform the actions. Let's examine how he argues this from the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: first the claim, then the two aspects of scriptural evidence, then the clarification about divine creation.
The passage is compact but contains a full argument.
2
Identify the two scriptural aspects
Maturidi mentions two aspects of revelation: command/prohibition and promise/threat. Find where he introduces these and how he supports each with Quranic verses.
The verses are partially quoted; focus on the reasoning.
3
Understand the clarification
After presenting the evidence, Maturidi addresses a potential objection: attributing actions to God does not negate human agency. He explains that God creates the actions, but humans earn and perform them.
This is a key point reconciling divine omnipotence with human responsibility.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that affirming human action denies divine creation. Maturidi's response shows that both are true: God creates, humans earn.
This is a central tenet of Maturidi theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله : وعندنا لازم تحقيق الفعل لهم بالسمع والعقل والضرورة التي يصير دافع ذلك مكابرا. فأما السمع فله وجهان الأمر به والنهي عنه، والثاني الوعيد فيه والوعد له، على تسمية ذلك في كل هذا فعلاً من نحو قوله: اعملوا ما شئتم، وقوله: وافعلوا الخير، وفي الجزاء ويريهم الله أعمالهم حسرات عليهم، وقوله: جزاء بما كانوا يعملون، وقوله: فمن يعمل مثقال ذرة الآية، وغير ذلك مما أثبت لهم أسماء العمّال ولفعلهم أسماء الفعل بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد وليس في الإضافة إلى الله سبحانه نفي ذلك ; بل هى الله بأن خلقها على ما هي عليه وأوجدها بعد أن لم تكن، وللخلق على ما كسبوها وفعلوها.
The shaykh (may God have mercy on him) said: According to us, the realization of the act for them is necessary by revelation, reason, and necessity, which whoever rejects becomes obstinate. As for revelation, it has two aspects: commanding it and prohibiting it, and the second is threat concerning it and promise for it, on the naming of that in all this as 'act' from such as His statement: "Do whatever you will," and His statement: "Do good," and concerning recompense: "And God will show them their deeds as regrets upon them," and His statement: "As recompense for what they used to do," and His statement: "Whoever does an atom's weight of good"—the verse, and other than that which fixed for them the names of 'workers' and for their actions the names of 'act' by command, prohibition, promise, and threat. And in the attribution to God the Exalted there is no negation of that; rather, it is God that He created them as they are and brought them into existence after they were not, and for the creatures according to what they earned and did.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents Maturidi's own position and the scriptural evidence. He asserts that actions must be truly attributed to humans based on revelation, reason, and necessity. He then explains revelation (sam') has two aspects: command/prohibition, and promise/threat. In scripture, God addresses humans with commands like 'Do whatever you will' and 'Do good', and threatens or promises based on their deeds. These addresses only make sense if humans genuinely perform the actions. Moreover, these scriptural texts give humans the name 'workers' and their actions the name 'acts'. This does not negate that God creates the actions and brings them into existence; rather, God creates the actions, but the humans have earned and performed them. Thus, the scriptural evidence supports the reality of human agency without compromising divine creation.

Key Terms
السمع
الأمر والنهي
الوعد والوعيد
تحقيق الفعل
كسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that affirming human action denies that God creates all actions.
Correction: Maturidi teaches that God creates actions, but humans earn and perform them; both are true simultaneously.

Checkpoint
What are the two aspects of scriptural evidence Maturidi presents?
A) Reason and necessity
B) Command/prohibition and promise/threat
C) Creation and earning
D) Tawhid and prophethood

Key Takeaway
Scriptural commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats logically require that human actions are genuine, while divine creation of those actions remains intact.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that God commands and prohibits, do you truly feel addressed as a responsible agent? How often do your actions align with that awareness? Today, before every action, pause and ask: Is this something God has commanded or prohibited? Commit to one change.
?
Imagine that every deed you do will be shown to you as regrets or rewards. Would that change how you live today? What is one specific habit you will begin to change right now, knowing that your actions are truly your own and will be recompensed?
