Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
Rational Proof that Human Actions Are Truly Theirs
Maturidi provides three rational proofs for human agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational arguments that establish genuine human agency, showing that divine commands, moral attribution, and reward/punishment are meaningless without real human action.

Core Idea
Without real human action, God's commands and justice become absurd.

Maturidi presents three rational arguments to affirm that humans are true agents of their actions. He begins with the logical necessity behind divine commands, then moves to the impossibility of attributing sin to God, and concludes with the coherence of reward and punishment. This passage grounds human responsibility in reason itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the three distinct arguments presented.
The passage is continuous; focus on the logical flow.
2
Identify the first argument: from command
Maturidi argues that commanding someone who has no capacity to act is impossible. He quotes the Quran and gives a reductio ad absurdum about commanding for the past.
3
Identify the second argument: from rational ugliness
It is rationally ugly (qabih) to attribute sin and disobedience to God. Since God is not the one who disobeys, actions must belong to humans.
4
Identify the third argument: from reward and punishment
God promises reward for obedience and punishment for disobedience. If God were the agent of both, He would be rewarding/punishing Himself, which is impossible. So actions must be human.
5
Reflect on the combined force
Consider how these three arguments together prove that human actions are truly theirs, preserving divine justice and meaningful command.
This counters the misconception that human agency diminishes God's power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أن الله إذ أمر ونهي، ومحال الأمر بما لا فعل فيه للمأمور أو النهي. قال الله تعالى : إن الله يأمر بالعدل والإحسان الآية، ولو جاز الأمر بذلك بلا معنى الفعل في الحقيقة لجاز اليوم الأمر بشيء يكون لأمس أو للعام الأول أو بإنشاء الخلائق، وإن كان لا معنى لذلك في أمر الخلق. ثم في العقل قبيح أن تضاف إلى الله الطاعة والمعصية وارتكاب الفواحش والمناكير وأنه المأمور المنهى المثاب المعاقب ، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له. ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأيضاً إن الله تعالى إنما وعد الثواب لمن أطاعه في الدنيا والعقاب لمن عصاه، فإذا كان الأمران فعله فإذا هو المَجْزي بما ذكر ; وإذا كان الثواب والعقاب حقيقة فالائتمار والانتهاء كذلك . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وكذلك في أنه محال أن يأمر أحد نفسه أو يطيعها أو
Moreover, that God commands and prohibits, and it is impossible to command something in which the commanded has no action or prohibition. God the Exalted said: 'Indeed God commands justice and excellence'—the verse. And if commanding that were permissible without meaning of action in reality, then it would be permissible today to command something that would be for yesterday or for the first year or for the creation of creatures, even if there is no meaning for that in the command of creation. Then in reason, it is ugly to attribute to God obedience and disobedience and committing indecencies and abominations, and that He is the commanded, the prohibited, the rewarded, the punished. So it is invalid that the act from these aspects be His. And there is no power except with God. And also, God the Exalted only promised reward to whomever obeyed Him in the world and punishment to whomever disobeyed Him. So if both matters were His act, then He would be the recompensed for what was mentioned; and if reward and punishment are real, then obeying and refraining are likewise. And there is no power except with God. And likewise, that it is impossible that one command oneself or obey oneself or...
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage provides a rational argument that human actions cannot be solely God's. Maturidi begins with an observation: God commands and prohibits, but it is impossible to command someone who has no capacity to act. If humans had no real action, commanding would be meaningless, like commanding something for the past. Therefore, humans must have real action. Next, he argues from reason: it is ugly (qabih) to attribute sin, disobedience, and indecency to God. If all actions were God's, then He would be the one commanded and prohibited, which is absurd. Since God is not the one who disobeys, the actions must belong to humans. Finally, he presents the argument from reward and punishment: God promises reward for obedience and punishment for disobedience. If God were the agent of both the obedience and disobedience, then He would be rewarding and punishing Himself, which is impossible. Since reward and punishment are real, the actions that earn them must be real and truly belong to humans. Thus, reason confirms that humans have genuine agency.

Key Terms
العقل
الأمر والنهي
الثواب والعقاب
قبيح
الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming human agency diminishes God's power and sovereignty.
Correction: Maturidi argues that human agency is necessary for divine commands, justice, and moral responsibility to be meaningful. This does not diminish God's power but rather makes His actions of commanding and rewarding coherent.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi consider it impossible for God to be the direct agent of all actions?
A) Because God is too exalted to create evil.
B) Because then God would be commanding and punishing Himself.
C) Because humans have independent power to create.
D) Because Quranic verses explicitly deny it.

Key Takeaway
Human actions are truly theirs, otherwise divine commands, moral responsibility, and reward and punishment become irrational.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your sins are your own, or do you secretly blame your circumstances, upbringing, or even God? How does this lesson challenge you to take full ownership of your actions?
?
If God’s commands are meaningful only because you can act, are you treating His commands as personally addressed to you, or as distant rules for others? What would change if you took every command as a direct call to action today?
?
The lesson shows that attributing sin to God is 'ugly.' Are there ways you have subtly blamed God for your failures? Will you repent and acknowledge that your choices are yours, and then seek His help to change?

Divine Decree
beginner
4 min
Scriptural Proof: Actions Are Attributed to Humans
Maturidi enumerates scriptural commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats as evidence that actions are named after humans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi uses Qur'anic commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats to prove that human actions are acquired by humans while created by God.

Core Idea
Scripture calls human deeds 'actions' even though God creates them.

This lesson examines the first part of Maturidi's proof, which draws directly from revelation. The Qur'an repeatedly commands and prohibits humans, and promises reward or threatens punishment for their deeds. This language would be meaningless unless humans have a real role in performing those actions. Maturidi shows that such scriptural references affirm human agency without denying God's creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the scriptural passage
Read the Arabic passage on scriptural proof. Notice the two aspects: command/prohibition and promise/threat.
2
Identify the two aspects
Maturidi identifies two aspects of revelation concerning actions: command/prohibition and promise/threat. Find where he states this.
3
Understand the complementarity
Notice that Maturidi says actions are attributed to God as creator and to humans as acquirers. This is not a contradiction but a complement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما السمع فله وجهان الأمر به والنهي عنه، والثاني الوعيد فيه والوعد له، على تسمية ذلك في كل هذا فعلاً من نحو قوله: اعملوا ما شئتم [فصلت، 40] وقوله: وافعلوا الخير [الحج، 77]؛ وفي الجزاء ويريهم الله أعمالهم حسرات عليهم [البقرة، 167]، وقوله: جزاء بما كانوا يعملون [السجدة، 17]، وقوله: فمن يعمل مثقال ذرة [الزلزال، 7] الآية، وغير ذلك مما أثبت لهم أسماء العمّال ولفعلهم أسماء الفعل بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد وليس في الإضافة إلى الله سبحانه نفي ذلك؛ بل هي الله بأن خلقها على ما هي عليه وأوجدها بعد أن لم تكن، وللخلق على ما كسبوها وفعلوها. على أن الله إذ أمر ونهي، ومحال الأمر بما لا فعل فيه للمأمور أو النهي. قال الله تعالى: إن الله يأمر بالعدل والإحسان الآية، ولو جاز الأمر بذلك بلا معنى الفعل في الحقيقة لجاز اليوم الأمر بشيء يكون لأمس أو للعام الأول أو بإنشاء الخلائق، وإن كان لا معنى لذلك في أمر الخلق. ثم في العقل قبيح أن تضاف إلى الله الطاعة والمعصية وارتكاب الفواحش والمناكير وأنه المأمور المنهى المثاب المعاقب، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
As for the [divine] transmission (al-sam'), it has two aspects: the command to do it and the prohibition from it, and the second is the threat regarding it and the promise for it, according to the naming of that in all these as an action, from His saying: 'Do what you will' [Fussilat, 40] and His saying: 'And do good' [al-Hajj, 77]; and regarding recompense: 'And God will show them their deeds as regrets' [al-Baqarah, 167], and His saying: 'Recompense for what they used to do' [al-Sajdah, 17], and His saying: 'So whoever does an atom's weight' [al-Zalzalah, 7] and the rest of the verse, and other than that by which He established for them the names of doers and for their actions the names of actions through command and prohibition and promise and threat. And there is no negation in attributing that to God, the Exalted; rather, they are God by His creating them as they are and bringing them into existence after they were not, and for the creation according to what they have acquired and done. [This is] because when God commands and prohibits, it is impossible to command that in which the commanded has no action or prohibition. God Almighty said: 'Indeed, God commands justice and excellence' and the rest of the verse. And if commanding that were permissible without the meaning of action in reality, then it would be permissible today to command something that was for yesterday or for the first year, or to command the creation of beings, even though there is no meaning for that in the command to creation. Then in reason, it is ugly to attribute obedience and disobedience and commission of abominations and evils to God, and [to say] that He is the commanded, the prohibited, the rewarded, the punished. So it is invalidated that the action is from Him in these respects. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a combined scriptural and rational proof that actions are attributed to humans as acquirers (kāsib) and to God as creator (khāliq). The author begins by identifying two aspects of divine revelation (al-sam') concerning actions: commands/prohibitions and promises/threats. He cites several Qur'anic verses that use the word 'action' (fi'l) in relation to humans, showing that scripture refers to human deeds as actions. He then states that this does not negate attributing actions to God as creator; rather, actions are attributed to God in terms of creation (khalq) and to humans in terms of acquisition (kasb) and performance. The author then provides a rational argument: it is impossible to command or prohibit something when the commanded has no ability to act in that matter. To illustrate, he says that if commanding were valid without real action, then one could command something for the past, which is absurd. Therefore, commands and prohibitions imply that humans have real agency. Next, using reason ('aql), he argues that it is ugly (qabīḥ) to attribute obedience, disobedience, and vile actions to God, because that would entail describing God with attributes proper to servants, such as being commanded, prohibited, rewarded, or punished. Since these cannot apply to God, the action cannot be from Him in that sense. Thus the doctrine that all actions are directly from God is invalidated. The refrain 'lā ḥawla wa lā quwwata illā billāh' emphasizes reliance on God.

Key Terms
السمع (al-sam')
الأمر (al-amr)
النهي (al-nahy)
الوعد (al-wa'd)
الوعيد (al-wa'īd)
الفعل (al-fi'l)
الكسب (al-kasb)
الخلق (al-khalq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates actions, then humans have no real part, making commands and threats meaningless.
Correction: Maturidi shows that scripture itself attributes actions to humans, indicating real human agency consistent with divine creation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi in this passage, what are the two aspects of revelation (al-sam') concerning actions?
A) Command and prohibition only
B) Promise and threat only
C) Command/prohibition and promise/threat
D) Creation and acquisition

Key Takeaway
Scripture uses command, prohibition, promise, and threat to affirm that humans are genuine agents of their actions even as God creates those actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you do a good deed, do you see it as solely your achievement, or do you acknowledge that God created the action and enabled you to do it? How does this lesson shift your gratitude and humility?
?
Think of a sin you committed recently. In light of this lesson, you cannot escape responsibility by saying 'God created it' because the action is attributed to you as your acquisition. Does this truth make you more fearful of disobedience and more eager to seek forgiveness?
?
If you truly believe that God creates every action—good and bad—and that you are still held accountable for what you acquire (kasb), how would that change the way you plan your day tomorrow?

Divine Decree
beginner
5 min
Rational Proof: Commands Imply Human Agency
Maturidi presents two rational proofs: the impossibility of command without action, and the ugliness of attributing sin to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational arguments that commands and prohibitions logically require human ability to act, and that attributing all actions to God alone leads to absurdities.

Core Idea
Reason shows that commanding without ability is impossible; thus humans have real agency.

Having established scriptural support for human acquisition, Maturidi now turns to rational arguments. He first argues that it is impossible to command or prohibit someone who has no ability to comply. If commands were valid without actual human action, then one could command something in the past, which is absurd. Additionally, it is rationally ugly to attribute disobedience and evil actions to God, because that would involve describing God with attributes of servants. These rational proofs reinforce the necessity of human agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the rational argument
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'على أن الله إذ أمر ونهي' through the end. Pay attention to the logical structure.
2
Understand the impossibility of command without action
Maturidi argues that commanding something that the commanded has no ability to do is impossible. Consider why this is self-evident.
3
Grasp the reductio ad absurdum
If commanding without action were allowed, one could command past events, which is absurd. This proves commands entail real human action.
4
Learn the rational ugliness argument
Using reason, Maturidi states it is qabīḥ (ugly) to attribute obedience/disobedience to God, because that would make God subject to commands and punishment. Therefore actions cannot be solely from God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما السمع فله وجهان الأمر به والنهي عنه، والثاني الوعيد فيه والوعد له، على تسمية ذلك في كل هذا فعلاً من نحو قوله: اعملوا ما شئتم [فصلت، 40] وقوله: وافعلوا الخير [الحج، 77]؛ وفي الجزاء ويريهم الله أعمالهم حسرات عليهم [البقرة، 167]، وقوله: جزاء بما كانوا يعملون [السجدة، 17]، وقوله: فمن يعمل مثقال ذرة [الزلزال، 7] الآية، وغير ذلك مما أثبت لهم أسماء العمّال ولفعلهم أسماء الفعل بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد وليس في الإضافة إلى الله سبحانه نفي ذلك؛ بل هي الله بأن خلقها على ما هي عليه وأوجدها بعد أن لم تكن، وللخلق على ما كسبوها وفعلوها. على أن الله إذ أمر ونهي، ومحال الأمر بما لا فعل فيه للمأمور أو النهي. قال الله تعالى: إن الله يأمر بالعدل والإحسان الآية، ولو جاز الأمر بذلك بلا معنى الفعل في الحقيقة لجاز اليوم الأمر بشيء يكون لأمس أو للعام الأول أو بإنشاء الخلائق، وإن كان لا معنى لذلك في أمر الخلق. ثم في العقل قبيح أن تضاف إلى الله الطاعة والمعصية وارتكاب الفواحش والمناكير وأنه المأمور المنهى المثاب المعاقب، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
As for the [divine] transmission (al-sam'), it has two aspects: the command to do it and the prohibition from it, and the second is the threat regarding it and the promise for it, according to the naming of that in all these as an action, from His saying: 'Do what you will' [Fussilat, 40] and His saying: 'And do good' [al-Hajj, 77]; and regarding recompense: 'And God will show them their deeds as regrets' [al-Baqarah, 167], and His saying: 'Recompense for what they used to do' [al-Sajdah, 17], and His saying: 'So whoever does an atom's weight' [al-Zalzalah, 7] and the rest of the verse, and other than that by which He established for them the names of doers and for their actions the names of actions through command and prohibition and promise and threat. And there is no negation in attributing that to God, the Exalted; rather, they are God by His creating them as they are and bringing them into existence after they were not, and for the creation according to what they have acquired and done. [This is] because when God commands and prohibits, it is impossible to command that in which the commanded has no action or prohibition. God Almighty said: 'Indeed, God commands justice and excellence' and the rest of the verse. And if commanding that were permissible without the meaning of action in reality, then it would be permissible today to command something that was for yesterday or for the first year, or to command the creation of beings, even though there is no meaning for that in the command to creation. Then in reason, it is ugly to attribute obedience and disobedience and commission of abominations and evils to God, and [to say] that He is the commanded, the prohibited, the rewarded, the punished. So it is invalidated that the action is from Him in these respects. And there is no power except with God.

Commentary
This passage is a combined scriptural and rational proof that actions are attributed to humans as acquirers (kāsib) and to God as creator (khāliq). Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that if God commands, He could still be the sole actor without human agency.
Correction: Maturidi shows rationally that commands logically require real human agency, else commands would be meaningless or impossible.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's rational argument, what would be the consequence if commanding were valid without real human action?
A) Commands would be easier to fulfill
B) One could command past events
C) Humans would still be responsible
D) God would not need to command

Key Takeaway
Reason demonstrates that divine commands necessarily imply human ability, and attributing all actions to God alone is rationally untenable because it would imply God is subject to command and punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever secretly think 'it was written for me' or 'God made me do it'? How does this lesson expose that excuse as a form of evading your own responsibility? Will you confess to yourself today that your sin is your choice?
?
Maturidi says it is rationally ugly to attribute sin to God. Yet, when you fail in obedience, how often do you shift blame to circumstances or to God's decree? What would it cost you to accept that your actions are your own?
?
If God's command proves you have the ability to obey, what does your disobedience say about your priorities? Will you stop telling yourself 'I can't' and start asking 'Why don't I want to?'

Divine Decree
intermediate
5 min
Reward and Punishment Require Human Agency
Maturidi refutes the doctrine of compulsion (Jabr) by exposing its absurd consequence regarding divine reward and punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses the reality of reward and punishment to argue against the doctrine of divine compulsion (Jabr) and to establish human agency.

Core Idea
Reward and punishment only make sense if humans truly perform actions.

This passage presents Maturidi's concise rational argument against the view that God creates all human actions. It hinges on a simple observation: if God were the doer of both obedience and disobedience, then reward and punishment would apply to God, not to humans. Maturidi concludes that human compliance and abstention must be genuine acts of the servant.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how brief and direct the argument is.
The passage is a single logical argument in a few lines.
2
Identify the premises and conclusion
Break down the argument: premise (God promises reward/punishment for obedience/disobedience), conditional (if both are God's acts), conclusion (then God would be the recompensed, which is absurd).
Maturidi uses an implicit reductio ad absurdum.
3
Reflect on the implication for human agency
Since reward and punishment are real for the servant, compliance and abstention must also be real human acts. This refutes the Jabri claim that God creates all actions.
This is a key argument in Maturidi's theology of free will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً إن الله تعالى إنما وعد الثواب لمن أطاعه في الدنيا والعقاب لمن عصاه، فإذا كان الأمران فعله فإذا هو المجزي بما ذكر؛ وإذا كان الثواب والعقاب حقيقة فالائتمار والانتهاء كذلك. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And also, God Almighty only promised reward to whoever obeyed Him in the world and punishment to whoever disobeyed Him. So if both matters are His act, then He would be the recompensed for what was mentioned. And if reward and punishment are real [for the servant], then compliance and abstention are likewise [real for the servant]. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a brief rational proof against the deterministic view (Jabr). It observes that God promises reward (thawāb) for obedience and punishment ('iqāb) for disobedience. The argument is: if both obedience and disobedience were solely God's creation and action, then God Himself would be the one receiving reward or punishment, which is impossible. However, reward and punishment are attributed to the servant in reality. Therefore, the actions of compliance (al-i'timār) and abstention (al-intihā') must be genuine acts of the servant, not merely metaphorical or divinely compelled. The conclusion is that the human truly performs these actions, and the divine promise and threat are meaningful only if humans have real agency.

Key Terms
الثواب (thawāb)
العقاب ('iqāb)
الائتمار (al-i'timār)
الانتهاء (al-intihā')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God compels all human actions and still punishes people for them.
Correction: If God compelled both obedience and disobedience, He would be the one deserving punishment or reward, which is impossible. Therefore humans must truly act.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that the doctrine of compulsion (jabr) is inconsistent with divine reward and punishment?
A) Because reward and punishment are not real.
B) Because if God creates both obedience and disobedience, then God would be the one deserving reward or punishment.
C) Because humans do not actually do anything.
D) Because reward and punishment are only in the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
The reality of divine reward and punishment proves that human actions are truly their own, not merely created by God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly feel that you are the one who chose to disobey, or do you sometimes attribute your actions to God's decree? How does that affect your repentance? Today, commit to taking full responsibility for your next action, good or bad.
?
If you believe that every action is directly created by God, how can you genuinely thank Him for your good deeds or seek forgiveness for your sins? Reflect on the logical consequences of Jabr and ask yourself: Does your heart truly accept that you are responsible?
?
Imagine standing before God on the Day of Judgment as He shows you the record of your deeds. Would you accept being rewarded or punished for actions you never truly did? How does this lesson's argument strengthen your conviction that you are the author of your choices? Let that conviction guide you in your next decision.

Divine Decree

The Absurdity of God Being Subject to Command and Having Opposite Attributes
Al-Maturidi shows that if God were the sole agent, then He would be both lord and servant, which is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing all human actions directly to God leads to the absurd conclusion that God would be both Lord and servant, which is impossible by reason and scripture.

Core Idea
God cannot be both commander and commanded; that would make Him both Lord and servant.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi presents a powerful reductio ad absurdum against the view that God is the sole agent of all actions. He shows that such a view would force us to say that God commands Himself, obeys Himself, and disobeys Himself—and that He would be both the Lord and the servant, the Creator and the created. This is impossible by both scripture and reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with a general impossibility before applying it to God.
2
Identify the initial impossibility
The passage states that it is impossible for someone to command, obey, or disobey themselves. Why? Because these actions require distinct parties. Understand this logical principle.
This is a rational judgment: a command implies a commander and a commanded.
3
See the consequence for God
If God were the sole agent of all actions, then the names 'servant', 'obedient', 'disobedient' would apply to God in reality. That would make God both Lord and servant, Creator and created.
This is the absurd conclusion that Maturidi draws.
4
Note the rejection by reason and scripture
Maturidi points out that this conclusion is rejected by both scripture (sam') and reason ('aql). Understand that this argument shows why the Jabri position is untenable.
The phrase 'wa lā quwwata illā billāh' emphasizes reliance on God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك في أنه محال أن يأمر أحد نفسه أو يطيعها أو يعصيها .. ومحال تسمية الله عبدا ذليلا مطيعا عاصيا سفيها جائرا، وقد سمّى الله تعالى بهذا كله أولئك الذين أمرهم ونهاهم. فإذا صارت هذه الأسماء في التحقيق له فيكون هو الرب وهو العبد وهو الخالق والمخلوق، ولا غير ثمة، وذلك مدفوع في السمع والعقل. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And likewise, it is impossible that one commands himself or obeys himself or disobeys himself. And it is impossible to name God a lowly servant, obedient, disobedient, foolish, unjust. And God has named with all of that those whom He commanded and prohibited. So if these names become in reality attributable to Him, then He would be the Lord and He would be the servant, He would be the Creator and He would be the created, and there would be nothing else. And that is rejected by scripture and reason. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage presents another reductio ad absurdum against the notion that all human actions are directly from God. The author first states that it is impossible for someone to command, obey, or disobey themselves, as these relations require distinct parties. If God were the sole agent of all actions, then there would be no real distinction between the commander and the commanded, which is absurd. Moreover, God has applied names like 'servant', 'obedient', 'disobedient', 'foolish', 'unjust' to humans in revelation. If those names were in reality attributable to God, then God would simultaneously be both Lord (Rab) and servant ('Abd), Creator (Khāliq) and created (Makhluq), which is impossible. Such a consequence is rejected by both scripture (sam') and reason ('aql). The argument shows that the Jabri position leads to a logical contradiction, thereby proving that the actions referred to by these names must be genuinely attributable to humans, not to God.

Key Terms
محال (muhāl)
العبد (al-'abd)
الرب (al-rabb)
الخالق (al-khāliq)
المخلوق (al-makhluq)
السمع (al-sam')
العقل (al-'aql)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God can be described by any attribute, including those of created beings like servanthood and disobedience.
Correction: This passage shows that attributing such names to God leads to the impossible conclusion that God would be both Lord and servant, Creator and created, which is rejected by both reason and revelation.

Checkpoint
What is the absurd conclusion Maturidi draws from the claim that all actions are from God?
A) That God would be both the commander and the commanded.
B) That God would be unjust.
C) That humans would not exist.
D) That God would have no attributes.

Key Takeaway
God cannot be described with opposites that would make Him both Lord and servant; this is impossible by reason and revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'God made me do it' or 'It's my nature' to avoid full responsibility? How does this passage challenge that evasion? Will you from now on own your disobedience fully before God?
?
The passage says it is impossible for God to be described as 'disobedient'. Yet every day, Muslims disobey Him. Does that make you feel the weight of your actions? How will you change your relationship with your Lord, knowing that you are the servant and He is the Master?
?
If you truly believed that your obedience or disobedience is solely your own doing and not God's, would your repentance be more urgent and sincere? Commit today to stop blaming anything or anyone else for your sins and turn to God with full accountability.

The Self-Knowledge Proof of Human Agency
Al-Maturidi presents self-knowledge as proof of human agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Maturidi uses self-evident self-knowledge to prove that humans are free agents, and why denying this would undermine all sensory knowledge.

Core Idea
Every person knows from themselves that they are a chooser and doer of their actions.

Al-Maturidi begins with a fundamental premise: each person has immediate, undeniable self-knowledge that they are a chooser and agent of their actions. This knowledge is as certain as sensory perception. In this lesson, we will examine this proof and its implication that the Jabriyya position is equivalent to rejecting sensory experience.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Al-Maturidi asserts self-knowledge as a basis for human agency.
2
Identify the three terms of agency
The passage uses three Arabic terms to describe human agency: مختار (chooser), فاعل (doer), and كاسب (acquirer). Find these in the text and understand their significance.
3
Understand the argument from sensory invalidation
Al-Maturidi argues that denying this self-knowledge would invalidate all sensory knowledge. Reflect on why this is a strong reductio ad absurdum.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا إن كل أحد يعلم من نفسه أنه مختار لما يفعله، وأنه فاعل كاسب، فلو جاز صرف مثله مما طريق العلم به الحس و إبطاله [لجاز إبطال جميع الحسيات] نحو العلم لجميع العالم، وذلك مهجور، فمثله قول أهل الجبر . وهذا قول يغنى الحكاية عن الإطناب فيه، لما ليس له كثير أتباع، ولما ليس لهذا القول معنى تكلم عليه صاحبه ؛ إذ هو ينفي عن نفسه حقيقة كل قول وفعل ، وإذا انتفى بطل القول، وبه يناظر ويُحاج، فزال الذي به يكون الحجاج واضمحل. ومن الناس من عارضهم، عند ظنهم وقوع التشابه ، بالعلم والوجود والكون وغير ذلك، وذلك لازم لو كان ثمة عقل يحتمل الإدراك، ولكنهم قوم أنكروا علم الضروريات وما هو في حد العيان، فلا معنى لمناظرتهم. ولا قوة إلا بالله . ـ ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق ونفي عنه التدبير فيها، وأزال عنه قدرة خلقها، وصير مشيئته فيها كبعض ما تتمنى به الأنفس أن قد تكون حقائق الأشياء خارجة منها واحتجوا في ذلك بالأمر والنهي ثم الوعد والوعيد ومحال رجوع مثله إلى ما للآمر والناهي حقيقته أو عليه وعيده وله وعده على ما ذكرنا وتلوا [في] ذلك آيات الأمر والنهي وذكر الفعل ثم آيات الجزاء؛ وهي بيّنة بحمد الله لمن قرأ القرآن ثم هم
And also, every person knows from himself that he is a chooser of what he does, and that he is a doer and an acquirer. So if it were permissible to turn away the like of this from what is known by sense perception and to invalidate it, then it would be permissible to invalidate all sensory things, like the knowledge of all the world. And that is abandoned. So the like of it is the saying of the people of compulsion (ahl al-jabr). And this is a saying that the narration suffices from elaborating on it, because it does not have many followers, and because this saying has no meaning for its proponent to discuss; for it negates from itself the reality of every saying and action. And when reality is negated, the saying is invalidated, and by it (the saying) one argues and debates. So that by which argumentation occurs has disappeared and dissipated. And among people are those who opposed them, when they thought similitude occurred, by [the attributes of] knowledge, existence, and being (kawn) and other than that. And that is necessary if there were a mind capable of perception. But they are a people who denied the knowledge of necessities and what is in the realm of observation, so there is no point in debating them. And there is no power except with God. — And among them are those who affirmed actions to the creation and negated from them control (tadbīr) in them, and removed from them the power to create them, and made their will in them like some of what souls wish for, that perhaps the realities of things come from outside of them. And they argued in that by the command and prohibition, then the promise and threat, and it is impossible for the like of that to refer to what the commander and prohibiter has its reality or upon him is its threat and for him is its promise, as we mentioned. And they recited concerning that the verses of command and prohibition and the mention of action, then the verses of recompense; and they are clear, praise be to God, for whoever reads the Qur'an, then they...
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument and refutation. First, it presents a self-evident proof: every person knows from themselves that they are a chooser (mukhtār) of their actions, a doer (fā'il), and an acquirer (kāsib). This knowledge is obtained through sense perception and is necessary. Denying it would require invalidating all sensory knowledge, which is impossible. Therefore, the view of the Jabriyya (ahl al-jabr) is equivalent to abandoning sense perception. The author then dismisses the Jabriyya as a group with few followers and a position that self-destructs because it negates the reality of all speech and action, thereby removing the very basis of argumentation. Next, he mentions another group (possibly some theologians) who opposed the Jabriyya by using attributes like knowledge (al-'ilm), existence (al-wujūd), and being (al-kawn) as analogies for human actions. But Maturidi criticizes them because they deny necessary knowledge and the obvious, so debating them is pointless. Finally, he describes a third group (likely Ahl al-Sunna) who affirm that actions are from the creation (al-khalq) but deny them control (tadbīr) and power (qudra) of creation, and they argue using the very same scriptural commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats. The author appears to endorse this view, noting that these verses are clear for whoever reads the Qur'an. The text ends mid-sentence but conveys approval of this group's position.

Key Terms
الاختيار
الفاعل
الكاسب
الحس
الجبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Self-knowledge of agency is purely subjective and cannot serve as a rational proof.
Correction: Al-Maturidi argues that this knowledge is like sense perception—necessary and universal—making it a valid foundation for argument.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Maturidi, what do people know by necessary self-knowledge?
A) That they are created.
B) That they are agents who choose and perform their actions.
C) That God predestines everything.
D) That the Jabriyya are correct.

Key Takeaway
Human agency is self-evident; denying it invalidates all sensory knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a decision today, do you truly feel that you are the chooser, or do you sometimes hide behind 'it was written' to avoid responsibility? How does al-Maturidi's argument confront that excuse?
?
If your own sense of choice is as real as your sense of sight, why do you so often act as if your actions are forced by circumstances? What would change if you owned your choices completely?
?
Al-Maturidi says denying self-knowledge of agency collapses all knowledge. In what areas of your life have you denied your own agency, and what did that denial cost you?

The Self-Defeating Nature of Jabriyya and the Weakness of Their Opponents' Analogies
Al-Maturidi refutes Jabriyya and criticizes analogical opponents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Maturidi finds the Jabriyya position self-defeating and why he also criticizes those who opposed them using analogies from divine attributes.

Core Idea
The Jabriyya position negates the reality of all speech and action, destroying the very basis of argumentation.

After presenting the self-knowledge proof, Al-Maturidi dismisses the Jabriyya as a negligible sect whose position is logically self-destructive. He also critiques other theologians who attempted to refute them by drawing analogies between human actions and divine attributes, arguing that such opponents deny necessary knowledge and are thus not worth debating.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two groups criticized
The passage criticizes two groups: the Jabriyya themselves, and those who opposed them using attributes like knowledge, existence, and being.
2
Understand the criticism of Jabriyya
Al-Maturidi says the Jabriyya position has no meaning because it negates the reality of every saying and action. Reflect on how this makes all argumentation impossible.
3
Understand the criticism of analogical opponents
Some opponents used attributes as analogies, but Al-Maturidi says they denied necessary knowledge and the obvious, so debating them is pointless.

The Correct Doctrine: Affirming Actions while Negating Control and Power
Al-Maturidi endorses the view that actions are from creation but control is from God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct position on human actions according to Al-Maturidi: actions are affirmed to creation but control and creative power are negated, as supported by scripture.

Core Idea
Humans perform actions but God creates them and has full control.

Finally, Al-Maturidi presents the correct view: human actions are real and attributed to the creation, but control (tadbīr) and power to create are from God alone. This group uses scriptural commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats as evidence. In this lesson, we will examine this balanced position and its scriptural basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three negations
The passage mentions negating control (tadbīr), power of creation (qudrat khalqihā), and making will like wishes. Note these phrases.
2
Understand the affirmation of actions
The correct group affirms actions to the creation (haqqa al-af'āl lil-khalq). This means humans are real agents, but not independent creators.
3
Recognize the scriptural proof
They cite verses of command and prohibition (āmār wa-nahī) and verses of recompense (jazzā'). Understand that these imply human responsibility and divine accountability.

Next, he mentions another group (possibly some theologians) who opposed the Jabriyya by using attributes like knowledge (al-'ilm), existence (al-wujūd), and being (al-kawn) as analogies for human actions. But Maturidi criticizes them because they deny necessary knowledge and the obvious, so debating them is pointless. Finally, he describes a third group (likely Ahl al-Sunna) who affirm that actions are from the creation (al-khalq) but deny them control (tadbīr) and power (qudra) of creation, and they argue using the very same scriptural commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats. The author appears to endorse this view, noting that these verses are clear for whoever reads the Qur'an. The text ends mid-sentence but conveys approval of this group's position.

Misconception: Affirming human actions implies human independence from God.
Correction: Al-Maturidi clarifies that while actions are attributed to humans, control and creative power belong solely to God.

Two Modes of Attributing Actions to God: By Cause and By Trial
Maturidi explains two modes of attributing actions to God besides direct creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two modes of attributing actions to God (by cause and by trial) and how they preserve divine transcendence while acknowledging human agency.

Core Idea
Actions can be attributed to God indirectly — by cause or by trial — not just by direct creation.

Imam Maturidi addresses a subtle theological question: how can we say actions are from God when they are also performed by humans? He explains that the Quran attributes actions to God in two ways besides literal agency: by the chain of causes, and as a test for faith or disbelief. This lesson unpacks those two modes and their scriptural examples.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Learn about the group that affirmed human actions but denied human creative power, setting up the need for a nuanced attribution.
This group argued using command/prohibition and reward/punishment.
2
Learn the first mode: by cause
Actions are attributed to the one who has the causes, even if the reality of the act is not his. This includes commanding good and abandoning evil.
Example: a person may be said to have done an action because they were the proximate cause.
3
Learn the second mode: by trial
Actions are attributed to God as a test for affirmation (tasdiq) or denial (takdhib). Examples from the Quran show this.
The Quran increases faith for believers and filth for disbelievers – the same act attributed differently.
4
Review Quranic examples
Examine the examples given: Quran, supplication, people causing forgetfulness, idols leading astray, worldly life deception, ruins and birds.
These show attributions that are not literal agency.
5
Reflect on divine transcendence
Understand how this preserves God's transcendence while explaining scriptural attributions.
God is not directly causing evil or disbelief; He creates contexts of testing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ـ ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق ونفي عنه التدبير فيها، وأزال عنه قدرة خلقها، وصير مشيئته فيها كبعض ما تتمنى به الأنفس أن قد تكون حقائق الأشياء خارجة منها
واحتجوا في ذلك بالأمر والنهي ثم الوعد والوعيد ومحال رجوع مثله إلى ما للآمر والناهي حقيقته أو عليه وعيده وله وعده على ما ذكرنا وتلوا في ذلك آيات الأمر والنهي وذكر الفعل ثم آيات الجزاء؛ وهي بيّنة بحمد الله لمن قرأ القرآن
سوعدوا على ذلك بما بينا في فساد قول المجبرة.
وقالوا في الإضافة إلى الله : إنها تخرج على وجهين سوى حقيقة الفعل. أحدهما بالسبب الذي كان منه الأفعال، مع الأمر بالخيرات والتخلية من الشرور. وقد تضاف الأفعال إلى من له الأسباب وإن لم يكن حقيقتها له. ولا قوة إلا بالله . والثاني أن الإضافة إليه عند المحنة بما له بها حال التصديق والتكذيب، كما أضيف إلى القرآن زادهم إيمانا ورجستا، وإلى الدعاء أنه زادهم نفورا، وإلى القوم أن أنسوهم ذكر الله، وإلى الأصنام أن أضللن كثيرا من الناس بما عبدن؛ ذلك كانت أفعال أولئك، فمثله الإضافة إلى الله. وقد يُحتمل الأحوال كما أضيف إلى الدنيا الغرور وإلى زينتها بما هي تظهر ما يكون في مثله الغرور، وإن لم يكن منها حق الفعل. وكذا ما أضيف إلى القرى الخاوية على عروشها والطيور من النطق
And among them are those who affirmed actions for the creation but negated from it the management (tadbir) in them, and removed from it the ability (qudra) to create them, and made its will (mashi'a) in them like some of what souls desire, that perhaps the realities of things are external to them.
And they argued for that with [the existence of] command and prohibition, then promise and threat, and it is impossible for something like that to refer to what belongs to the commander and prohibiter in reality, or that His threat and His promise are upon Him? as we mentioned, and they recited in that the verses of command and prohibition and the mention of action, then the verses of recompense; and they are clear, praise be to God, for whoever reads the Quran.
They fortified themselves for that with what we have shown concerning the corruption of the statement of the Jabriyya.
And they said concerning attribution (idafa) to God: It occurs in two ways besides the reality of the act. One of them is by the cause (sabab) from which the acts originated, along with commanding to good things and abandoning evil things. And acts may be attributed to the one who has the causes even if the reality of them is not his. And there is no power except with God. The second is that attribution to Him is upon trial (mihnah) by what He has in that state of affirmation (tasdiq) and denial (takdhib), just as was attributed to the Quran: 'it increased them in faith and filth' [Quran 9:124-125], and to the supplication: 'it increased them in aversion' [Quran 71:5-6], and to the people: 'they made them forget the remembrance of God' [Quran 23:109-110], and to the idols: 'they have led many astray' [Quran 14:35-36]; that was the actions of those, so similarly is attribution to God. And states may be interpreted such as was attributed to the worldly life of deception and to its adornment as it shows what in its like is deception, even if the true act is not from it. And likewise what was attributed to the villages fallen down upon their roofs [Quran 2:259] and to the birds of speech [Quran 27:20-22].
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific group (possibly the Ash'ariyya or a related school) that affirms human actions (af'al) as real but denies humans the power of creating them (qudrat al-khalq). Instead, they view human will (mashi'a) as something like mere wishes. They support their view with the existence of divine command/prohibition and reward/punishment, arguing that these would be meaningless if humans were not agents in some sense. They also cite Quranic verses. The author then presents their position on attributing actions to God: there are two modes besides literal agency. The first is attribution by cause (sabab): actions are caused by a chain that ultimately goes back to God, but they are attributed to the one who has the proximate cause (e.g., a person through their choice). The second is attribution by trial (mihnah) or testing: some events are attributed to God because they serve as a test for affirmation (tasdiq) or denial (takdhib). Examples include the Quran increasing faith for believers and filth for disbelievers, or supplication increasing aversion. Similarly, attributions to worldly life (deception) and to ruins and birds (speech) are metaphorical, not literal agency. Thus, actions can be attributed to God in ways other than direct creation.

Correction: Maturidi shows that actions can be attributed to God indirectly by cause or trial, preserving divine transcendence.

Checkpoint

D) By essence and by attributes.

Key Takeaway
Attributing actions to God by cause or trial allows us to affirm divine sovereignty while preserving human responsibility.

?

Two Modes of Attributing Actions to God
Maturidi enumerates two modes of attributing actions to God besides their direct reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two modes of attributing actions to God according to Imam Maturidi — by cause and during trial — and how they differ from direct creation.

Core Idea
Not every attribution to God means direct creation; some are by cause or context.

Imam Maturidi addresses a crucial theological issue: when we say God does something, does it always mean He directly creates it? He explains that actions can be attributed to God in two ways besides direct creation. This distinction helps resolve apparent conflicts in the Quran and everyday language. Let's read his classification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the translation. Let the author's own structure come through.
Notice the phrase 'two ways' (وجهين) which sets the classification.
2
Identify the two modes
The passage explicitly lists two modes. Find where each is introduced and how they are defined.
The first mode uses 'بالسبب' and the second 'عند المحنة'.
3
Examine the examples
Maturidi provides several examples for the second mode from the Quran and common language. Notice how they illustrate attribution by context.
Examples include the Quran increasing faith/filth, supplication increasing flight, etc.
4
Understand the principle
The key principle is that attribution can be by cause (sabab) or by circumstance (miḥnah), not always direct creation. This avoids misunderstanding God's actions.
The closing 'There is no power except with God' reinforces dependence.
5
Reflect on the misconception
Consider how this passage corrects the mistaken belief that all divine attributions imply direct creation.
This is a common theological confusion addressed by Maturidi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالوا في الإضافة إلى الله: إنها تخرج على وجهين سوى حقيقة الفعل. أحدهما بالسبب الذي كان منه الأفعال، مع الأمر بالخيرات والتخلية من الشرور. وقد تضاف الأفعال إلى من له الأسباب وإن لم يكن حقيقتها له. ولا قوة إلا بالله. والثاني أن الإضافة إليه عند المحنة بما له بها حال التصديق والتكذيب، كما أضيف إلى القرآن زادهم إيمانا ورجسا، وإلى الدعاء أنه زادهم نفورا، وإلى القوم أن أنسوهم ذكر الله، وإلى الأصنام أن أضللن كثيرا من الناس بما عبدوا؛ ذلك كانت أفعال أولئك، فمثله الإضافة إلى الله. وقد يحتمل الأحوال كما أضيف إلى الدنيا الغرور وإلى زينتها بما هي تظهر ما يكون في مثله الغرور، وإن لم يكن منها حق الفعل. وكذا ما أضيف إلى القرى الخاوية على عروشها والطيور من النطق وإلى البهائم من الشكاية مما لو كانت تنطق بقول. فمثله في الإضافة إلى الله بما منه من الإمهال وإظهار النعم الذي كاد أن يكون حجة لهم في الرضا بأفعالهم؛ ولذلك ظنوا أن الله أمرهم بما هم فيه من الأفعال بالإمهال والتأخير. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And they said concerning attribution to God: It occurs in two ways besides the reality of the act. First, by the cause from which actions proceed, along with commanding good and leaving evil. And actions are attributed to the one who has the causes even if the reality of them is not his. And there is no power except with God. Second, that attribution to Him is during trial by what He has therein of states of belief and disbelief, just as it is attributed to the Quran that it increased them in faith and filth, and to the supplication that it increased them in flight, and to the people that they made them forget the remembrance of God, and to the idols that they led many people astray by what they worshipped; that was the actions of those, so similarly is attribution to God. And states may be carried as it is attributed to the world of deception and to its adornment in that it shows what in its like is deception, even if the reality of the act is not from it. And likewise what is attributed to the villages fallen upon their roofs, and to birds of speech, and to beasts of complaint such that if they were to speak they would say. So similarly in attribution to God includes the delaying and showing of blessings which almost became an argument for them in approving their actions; therefore they thought that God commanded them in what they are doing of actions by delaying and postponing. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification: Maturidi explains that the attribution of actions to God occurs in two distinct modes aside from the direct reality of the act (ḥaqīqat al-fiʿl). The first mode is by cause (sabab): God is the ultimate source from which actions originate, as He commands good and leaves evil, and actions are attributed to the one who has the causes even if the act is not directly his. The second mode is during trial (miḥnah): God attributes to Himself states like increase of faith or filth depending on the person's response, as in Quranic verses where the Quran increases believers in faith and disbelievers in filth, the prophet's call increases disbelievers in flight, people cause forgetfulness, and idols lead astray. These are the actions of those beings, so similarly attribution to God follows the same pattern. Maturidi then gives further examples from common language: the world is attributed with deception, villages with ruin, birds with speech, and beasts with complaint, even though these are not their direct acts. Similarly, attribution to God includes delaying punishment and showing blessings, which some people misinterpreted as God commanding them to do evil through delay. The passage ends with 'There is no power except with God,' emphasizing dependence on God. This clarifies that not all attributions imply direct creation; some are by cause or context.

Correction: Maturidi explains that attribution can be by cause or context, not necessarily direct creation.

Affirming Human Actions and the Duality of Kasb
Maturidi argues that actions belong to servants by acquisition and to God by creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that human actions are attributed to God as creation and to humans as acquisition, based on the necessity of differing aspects (jiha) when opposites are used.

Core Idea
Actions have two realities: God creates, humans acquire – a difference of aspect.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi engages with a theological problem: how can human actions be both created by God and freely responsible for humans? He identifies a group that affirms actions for creatures while also attributing them to God as creation. To resolve the apparent contradiction, he introduces the concept of aspect (jiha) – the same act can be viewed from two different vantage points. As you read, notice how he uses pairs of opposites to illustrate that dual attribution is necessary for logical coherence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the group Maturidi discusses
Read the opening sentence to understand that some theologians affirm actions for creatures (making them responsible) while also attributing those actions to God as creation. This sets up the problem of dual attribution.
This group likely refers to the Mu'tazila or a precursor view.
2
List the pairs of opposites
Maturidi provides a list of opposite attributions (e.g., misguidance/guidance, abandonment/protection). Notice that these are opposite in meaning and cannot be attributed to the same subject without a difference in aspect.
Each pair illustrates that the same act can be described from two sides.
3
Understand the logical inference
Maturidi argues that if something is attributed to God absolutely, its opposite must also be attributable to the relevant subject (the servant). The existence of both aspects validates the dual reality of the act.
This leads to the conclusion that the act has two distinct realities.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The passage ends with the statement that the act belongs to servants by acquisition (kasb) and to God by creation (khalq). This is the Maturidi doctrine of kasb.
The proof that follows is not included here, but the core argument is complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق، وبها صاروا عصاة تقاة، وجعلوها الله خلقا، اعتبارًا بما سبق من الإضافة إلى الله جل ثناؤه مرة وإلى العباد ثانيا. والمذكور المضاف إلى المضاف إلى الله تعالى لا غير؛ بمعنى يؤدي إلى اختلاف الجهة في الفعل؛ نحو الإضلال والإزاغة، والهداية والعصمة، ثم الإنعام والامتنان، ثم الخذلان والمد، ثم الزيادة من الوجهين، ثم الطبع والتيسير، ثم الشرح والتضييق. ومحال وجود هذه الأحوال على وجود مضادّات ما يوصف بها، وفي ذات الله إضافة الاهتداء والضلالة والرشد والغي والاستقامة والزيغ إلى الخلق؛ وكان في وجود أحد الوجهين تحقيق الآخر، إذ لا يضاف الذي أضيف إلى الله مطلقا مع عدم إضافة أضداد الواقع عليه معانيها. ثبت أن حقيقة ذلك الفعل الذي هو للعباد من طريق الكسب والله من طريق الخلق. دليل ذلك
And among them are those who affirmed the actions for the creation, and by them they became disobedient and pious, and they made them God's creation, considering the prior attribution to God, may His praise be exalted, once, and to the servants secondly. And the mentioned is attributed to the one to whom it is attributed, to God the Exalted exclusively; meaning that it leads to a difference of aspect in the act, such as misguidance and deviation, guidance and protection, then favor and grace, then abandonment and extension, then increase from both sides, then sealing and facilitating, then expansion and constriction. And it is impossible for these states to exist with the existence of opposites of what is described by them, and in God's essence is the attribution of guidance and misguidance, rectitude and error, uprightness and deviation to the creation; and in the existence of one of the two aspects is the realization of the other, for that which is attributed to God absolutely is not attributed without the attribution of the opposites which their meanings apply to it. It is established that the reality of that act which is for the servants is by way of acquisition and for God by way of creation. The proof of that...
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is an argument about the reality of human actions. Maturidi discusses a group (likely some sect) that affirms actions for creatures (al-khalq) and considers them obedient or disobedient by them, while also attributing those actions to God as creation. He notes that the dual attribution (to God and to servants) leads to a difference in aspect (jiha) of the act. He then lists pairs of opposite attributions: misguidance/deviation, guidance/protection, favor/grace, abandonment/extension, increase from both sides, sealing/facilitating, expansion/constriction. These pairs are contradictory and cannot exist together unless they have different aspects. He states that in God's essence (or by God's essence), the attribution of guidance and misguidance, etc., to the creatures also holds—meaning that both aspects are real. He argues that if something is attributed to God absolutely, its opposite must also be attributed to the relevant subject (i.e., the servant). The conclusion is that the reality of the act belongs to the servant by way of kasb (acquisition) and to God by way of khalq (creation). The passage ends with 'The proof of that' indicating a subsequent argument. This is the classic Maturidi doctrine of kasb, reconciling divine predestination and human responsibility.

الخلق

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that affirming human actions negates divine creation, or that attributing actions to both God and humans is a contradiction.
Correction: Maturidi resolves this by distinguishing between the aspect of creation (attributed to God) and the aspect of acquisition (attributed to humans). They are two sides of the same act.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that human actions are real acquisitions of humans and real creations of God, made possible by a difference in aspect (jiha).

The Dual Attribution of Actions and the Middle Path
Maturidi introduces the problem of dual attribution and states the doctrine of kasb and khalq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why actions are attributed both to God and to humans, and how this leads to the Maturidi doctrine of kasb and khalq.

Core Idea
Actions have two aspects: creation from God, acquisition from humans.

Imam Maturidi begins by addressing a critical theological problem: both the Quran and reason attribute actions to God as the Creator, yet also hold humans responsible. Some groups seized on one side to the exclusion of the other, leading to extremes. In this passage, Maturidi lays the foundation for a balanced understanding by showing that these dual attributions refer to different aspects of the same act.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Notice the flow from problem to solution.
Pay attention to the list of opposite pairs.
2
Identify the dual attributions
Maturidi lists several pairs of opposites attributed to both God and humans. Find them and note that they are opposites.
Examples: misguidance/guidance, expansion/restriction.
3
Understand the logical implication
Maturidi argues that opposites cannot coexist without a distinction in aspect. Reflect on why this forces a distinction between creation and acquisition.
This is the key move in the argument.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The passage concludes that the reality of the act is creation from God and acquisition from the servant. See how this avoids both extremes.
This establishes the Maturidi middle path.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق، وبها صاروا عصاة تقاة، وجعلوها الله خلقا، اعتبارًا بما سبق من الإضافة إلى الله جل ثناؤه مرة وإلى العباد ثانيا. والمذكور المضاف إلى المضاف إلى الله تعالى لا غير؛ بمعنى يؤدي إلى اختلاف الجهة في الفعل؛ نحو العباد هو الإضلال والإزاغة، والهداية والعصمة، ثم الإنعام والامتنان، ثم الخذلان والمد[؟] ثم الزيادة من الوجهين، ثم الطبع والتيسير، ثم الشرح والتضييق. ومحال وجود هذه الأحوال على وجود مضادّات ما يوصف بها، وفي ذات الله إضافة الاهتداء والضلالة، والرشد والغي، والاستقامة والزيغ إلى الخلق؛ وكان في وجود أحد الوجهين تحقيق الآخر، إذ لا يضاف الذي أضيف إلى الله مطلقا مع إضافة أضداد الواقع عليه معانيها. ثبت أن حقيقة ذلك الفعل الذي هو للعباد من طريق الكسب والله من طريق الخلق. دليل ذلك ان فعل الله تعالى في التحقيق خلقه، وكل ذلك لو أضيف إليه باسم الخلق لم يفهم منه في ذلك غير إنشاء، وفهم من الذي فهم من العبد فعله وكسبه نحو أن نقول: خلق الشرح والضيق، وخلق الضلال والاهتداء ونحو ذلك، فمثله الأول. ما لو جاز صرف أحد مع الوجهين عن حقيقة المفهوم أو صرفه إلى الأسباب أو الأحوال فالآخر مثله، وكل ذلك مجاز لا حقيقة. ولذلك جاء مقابلة القولين: الجبرية والقدرية، وهذا معنى ما روى من لعن المرجئة والقدرية. إن المرجئة أرجأت الأفعال إلى الله ولم تجعلها للعبد، والقدرية أثبتتها الله على ما ينسب الخلق إلى الله تعالى، ولم تجعل الله فيها تدبيرا. والعدل هو القول بتحقيق الأمرين، ليكون الله موصوفا بما وصف به نفسه محمودا به كما قال: خالق كل شيء، وقال: فهو على كل شيء قدير، وليكون عدلا مفصلا كما قال: وما ربك بظلام للعبيد، وقال: ولولا فضل الله عليكم ورحمته لا تبعتم الشيطان إلا قليلا. ثم الدليل على لزوم القول بهذا مع ما فيما بينا كفاية وجوه أحوال في أفعال العبد لا يبلغها أوهامهم ولا يقدرها عقولهم وأحوال فيها ينتهي إليها قصدهم وتبلغها عقولهم. فثبت أنها من الوجه الأول ليست لهم، ومن الوجه الثاني لهم. فالأول كتصوير خروج الشيء من العدم إلى الوجود
And among them are those who attributed actions to creation, and thereby they became disobedient and pious, and they made them God's creation, considering what preceded of attribution to God, exalted be His praise, once, and to servants, secondly. And the mentioned is attributed to the attributed to God Almighty only; meaning leading to difference of aspect in the act; such as the servant is misguidance and deviation, guidance and protection, then favor and grace, then abandonment and sustainability [؟], then increase from both sides, then sealing and facilitation, then expansion and restriction. And it is impossible that these states exist along with the existence of opposites of what is described by them, and in the essence of God is the attribution of guidance and misguidance, rectitude and error, uprightness and deviation to the creation; and in the existence of one of the two aspects is the realization of the other, since that which is attributed to God absolutely is not attributed without the attribution of opposites whose meanings are realized upon it. It is established that the reality of that act which belongs to servants by way of acquisition (kasb) and to God by way of creation (khalq). The proof of that is that the act of God Almighty in reality is His creation, and all of that, if attributed to Him by the name of creation, nothing is understood from that other than origination, and it is understood from what is understood from the servant his act and his acquisition, such as we say: He created expansion and restriction, and He created misguidance and guidance and the like, so the first is like it. If it were permissible to turn one with the two aspects away from the reality of the understood, or to turn it to causes or states, then the other is like it, and all of that is metaphorical, not real. Therefore, the two statements confront each other: Jabriyya (determinists) and Qadariyya (free-will advocates), and this is the meaning of what has been narrated of cursing the Murji'a and Qadariyya. The Murji'a deferred actions to God and did not make them for the servant, and the Qadariyya affirmed them to God according to what is attributed of creation to God Almighty, and did not make God have any disposal in them. And justice (al-'adl) is the statement of realizing both matters, so that God is described with what He described Himself, praised in it, as He said: 'Creator of everything' (6:102), and He said: 'He is over all things Omnipotent' (6:17), and so that it is a decisive justice, as He said: 'And your Lord is not unjust to His servants' (41:46), and He said: 'And if not for the grace of God upon you and His mercy, you would have followed Satan, except a few' (4:83). Then the proof of the necessity of saying this—with what we have already stated being sufficient—is aspects of states in the actions of the servant that their imaginations cannot reach nor their intellects measure, and states in which their intention ends and their intellects reach them. So it is established that from the first aspect they are not theirs, and from the second aspect they are theirs. The first is like the depiction of bringing a thing from non-existence to existence
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition by Imam Maturidi on the nature of human actions, defining the middle path between two extremes. It begins by noting a group that attributes actions entirely to the creation (i.e., Qadariyya), making humans the originators, and another that attributes them solely to God (Jabriyya). Maturidi points out that both extremes arise from considering only one side of the dual attribution found in revelation: actions are sometimes attributed to God and sometimes to servants. He then lists a series of dual attributes (e.g., misguidance and guidance, expansion and restriction) that are opposites and cannot coexist without a distinction in perspective. Since God's absolute attribution of these states to Himself would negate the possibility of opposite attributes being realized, it becomes necessary to distinguish between the creation (khalq) and the acquisition (kasb) of the act: God creates the act, and the servant acquires it. The proof is that when an act is called 'creation' (khalq), it implies mere origination from God; the same act, when considered from the human side, is understood as their act and acquisition. Shifting either perspective to a metaphorical interpretation would make the other likewise metaphorical, which would entail abandoning the literal truth of the Quranic attributes. The opposing schools—Jabriyya and Qadariyya—are thus refuted, with Maturidi referencing the tradition of cursing the Murji'a (who defer agency to God) and Qadariyya. The correct doctrine is 'justice' (al-'adl), which upholds both sides: God's creation of the act and human responsibility. This is supported by Quranic verses stating God's universal creation and power, and His justice in not wronging servants. Finally, a further proof is offered: some aspects of human actions are beyond human comprehension (like creation ex nihilo), while others are within their reach (like intention and choice). Thus, the act is not fully theirs from one viewpoint (creation) but is theirs from another (acquisition). The analogy of bringing something from non-existence to existence illustrates the creative aspect beyond human capacity.

Key Terms
الكسب (al-kasb)
الخلق (al-khalq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the reality of the act that belongs to both God and the servant?
A) It is entirely God's creation and the servant has no part.
B) It is entirely the servant's creation.
C) It is creation from God and acquisition from the servant.
D) It is a metaphor for both.

Key Takeaway
Actions have two real aspects: God's creation and human acquisition, which avoids the extremes of Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly acknowledge that you acquired that sin, or do you subtly blame God's decree for your failure? Confess honestly: have you ever used divine predestination as an excuse for your own negligence?
?
If every good action is ultimately created by God, why do you take pride in your piety or deeds? How does this lesson strip away your self-satisfaction and humble you before your Creator?
?
In your daily life, do you reflect on the distinction between God's creation and your acquisition? How would your repentance change if you truly believed that your sin is entirely your acquisition and entirely God's creation? What step will you take today to embody this middle path?

Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
Proof of Kasb and Khalq and Refutation of Extremes
Maturidi provides the conceptual proof for kasb and khalq and refutes Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conceptual proof that the same act is called 'creation' from God and 'acquisition' from humans, and how this refutes both determinism and libertarianism.

Core Idea
The terms 'creation' and 'acquisition' refer to the same act from different perspectives, not two separate acts.

Maturidi now provides a linguistic-conceptual proof: when we say God creates an act, we mean origination; when we say the human acquires it, we mean responsible performance. If we shift either to metaphor, the other would also be metaphorical, undermining the plain meaning of revelation. This proof directly confronts the errors of the Jabriyya and Qadariyya, as referenced in a prophetic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Study the proof from meaning
Maturidi argues that when an act is called 'creation' from God, it implies origination; when called 'acquisition' from humans, it implies responsible performance. These are literal understandings.
2
Understand the symmetry argument
If either attribution were taken metaphorically, then the other would also have to be metaphorical, because they are parallel. This would make all Quranic attributions metaphorical, which is untenable.
This is the core of the proof.
3
See how this refutes the extremes
Jabriyya deny any real human acquisition; Qadariyya deny God's creation of the act. Both are refuted by this proof, and the tradition cursing Murji'a and Qadariyya confirms the error.

Commentary

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi argue would happen if one of the two attributions (creation or acquisition) were taken metaphorically?
A) Only that attribution would be metaphorical.
B) The other would also be metaphorical.
C) The act would become impossible.
D) God would be unjust.

Key Takeaway
Both 'creation' and 'acquisition' are literal terms for the same act from different perspectives; making one metaphorical forces the other to be metaphorical, which is untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you naturally blame your circumstances or weaknesses (like a Jabri) as if God created you to sin, or do you deny His sovereignty over that act (like a Qadari) to protect your own image? Which tendency is stronger in your heart, and what will you do today to align your belief with the truth that you are both fully responsible and fully dependent on God?
?
If you truly believed that every single action you perform—good or bad—is created by God and acquired by you, would your attitude change? Would you take more ownership of your deeds or fall into despair? How can you use this lesson to shape your next sincere repentance?
?
Consider a recent good deed you did. Did you thank God for creating it and enabling you, or did you inwardly attribute it to your own merit? And a recent mistake: did you feel crushed by guilt or blame God? Based on this teaching, how can you hold both gratitude for God's creation and accountability for your acquisition in your heart from now on?

Divine Decree
intermediate

The Doctrine of 'Adl and the Duality of Human Actions
Maturidi defines 'adl as the correct doctrine and provides Quranic and rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi concept of 'adl as affirming both divine creation and human responsibility, supported by Quranic verses and a final proof from the nature of human actions.

Core Idea
God's justice requires that He creates all acts while humans are accountable for their acquisitions.

Having established the conceptual distinction between creation and acquisition, Maturidi defines this as the stance of 'adl (justice). This position is not a compromise but the correct understanding that allows God to be praised as Creator and humans to be justly rewarded or punished. Maturidi then provides a final proof: some aspects of human actions are beyond human power (creation ex nihilo) while others are within their capacity (intention and choice). Thus, the act is theirs from one perspective and not theirs from another.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of 'adl
Maturidi defines justice as 'realizing both matters' — affirming both God's creation and human acquisition. Read this section carefully.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
Maturidi cites verses that describe God as Creator of everything and as powerful, and others that affirm He does not wrong His servants and that His grace is essential.
These verses support both divine sovereignty and human responsibility.
3
Analyze the final proof
Maturidi presents a proof from the duality of human actions: some aspects are beyond human comprehension and power (like bringing from nothing), while others are within their intention and ability. Thus, the act is theirs from one aspect and not from another.
This reinforces the doctrine of kasb and khalq.
