⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق، وبها صاروا عصاة تقاة، وجعلوها الله خلقا، اعتبارًا بما سبق من الإضافة إلى الله جل ثناؤه مرة وإلى العباد ثانيا. والمذكور المضاف إلى المضاف إلى الله تعالى لا غير؛ بمعنى يؤدي إلى اختلاف الجهة في الفعل؛ نحو العباد هو الإضلال والإزاغة، والهداية والعصمة، ثم الإنعام والامتنان، ثم الخذلان والمد[؟] ثم الزيادة من الوجهين، ثم الطبع والتيسير، ثم الشرح والتضييق. ومحال وجود هذه الأحوال على وجود مضادّات ما يوصف بها، وفي ذات الله إضافة الاهتداء والضلالة، والرشد والغي، والاستقامة والزيغ إلى الخلق؛ وكان في وجود أحد الوجهين تحقيق الآخر، إذ لا يضاف الذي أضيف إلى الله مطلقا مع إضافة أضداد الواقع عليه معانيها. ثبت أن حقيقة ذلك الفعل الذي هو للعباد من طريق الكسب والله من طريق الخلق. دليل ذلك ان فعل الله تعالى في التحقيق خلقه، وكل ذلك لو أضيف إليه باسم الخلق لم يفهم منه في ذلك غير إنشاء، وفهم من الذي فهم من العبد فعله وكسبه نحو أن نقول: خلق الشرح والضيق، وخلق الضلال والاهتداء ونحو ذلك، فمثله الأول. ما لو جاز صرف أحد مع الوجهين عن حقيقة المفهوم أو صرفه إلى الأسباب أو الأحوال فالآخر مثله، وكل ذلك مجاز لا حقيقة. ولذلك جاء مقابلة القولين: الجبرية والقدرية، وهذا معنى ما روى من لعن المرجئة والقدرية. إن المرجئة أرجأت الأفعال إلى الله ولم تجعلها للعبد، والقدرية أثبتتها الله على ما ينسب الخلق إلى الله تعالى، ولم تجعل الله فيها تدبيرا. والعدل هو القول بتحقيق الأمرين، ليكون الله موصوفا بما وصف به نفسه محمودا به كما قال: خالق كل شيء، وقال: فهو على كل شيء قدير، وليكون عدلا مفصلا كما قال: وما ربك بظلام للعبيد، وقال: ولولا فضل الله عليكم ورحمته لا تبعتم الشيطان إلا قليلا. ثم الدليل على لزوم القول بهذا مع ما فيما بينا كفاية وجوه أحوال في أفعال العبد لا يبلغها أوهامهم ولا يقدرها عقولهم وأحوال فيها ينتهي إليها قصدهم وتبلغها عقولهم. فثبت أنها من الوجه الأول ليست لهم، ومن الوجه الثاني لهم. فالأول كتصوير خروج الشيء من العدم إلى الوجود
And among them are those who attributed actions to creation, and thereby they became disobedient and pious, and they made them God's creation, considering what preceded of attribution to God, exalted be His praise, once, and to servants, secondly. And the mentioned is attributed to the attributed to God Almighty only; meaning leading to difference of aspect in the act; such as the servant is misguidance and deviation, guidance and protection, then favor and grace, then abandonment and sustainability [؟], then increase from both sides, then sealing and facilitation, then expansion and restriction. And it is impossible that these states exist along with the existence of opposites of what is described by them, and in the essence of God is the attribution of guidance and misguidance, rectitude and error, uprightness and deviation to the creation; and in the existence of one of the two aspects is the realization of the other, since that which is attributed to God absolutely is not attributed without the attribution of opposites whose meanings are realized upon it. It is established that the reality of that act which belongs to servants by way of acquisition (kasb) and to God by way of creation (khalq). The proof of that is that the act of God Almighty in reality is His creation, and all of that, if attributed to Him by the name of creation, nothing is understood from that other than origination, and it is understood from what is understood from the servant his act and his acquisition, such as we say: He created expansion and restriction, and He created misguidance and guidance and the like, so the first is like it. If it were permissible to turn one with the two aspects away from the reality of the understood, or to turn it to causes or states, then the other is like it, and all of that is metaphorical, not real. Therefore, the two statements confront each other: Jabriyya (determinists) and Qadariyya (free-will advocates), and this is the meaning of what has been narrated of cursing the Murji'a and Qadariyya. The Murji'a deferred actions to God and did not make them for the servant, and the Qadariyya affirmed them to God according to what is attributed of creation to God Almighty, and did not make God have any disposal in them. And justice (al-'adl) is the statement of realizing both matters, so that God is described with what He described Himself, praised in it, as He said: 'Creator of everything' (6:102), and He said: 'He is over all things Omnipotent' (6:17), and so that it is a decisive justice, as He said: 'And your Lord is not unjust to His servants' (41:46), and He said: 'And if not for the grace of God upon you and His mercy, you would have followed Satan, except a few' (4:83). Then the proof of the necessity of saying this—with what we have already stated being sufficient—is aspects of states in the actions of the servant that their imaginations cannot reach nor their intellects measure, and states in which their intention ends and their intellects reach them. So it is established that from the first aspect they are not theirs, and from the second aspect they are theirs. The first is like the depiction of bringing a thing from non-existence to existence
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition by Imam Maturidi on the nature of human actions, defining the middle path between two extremes. It begins by noting a group that attributes actions entirely to the creation (i.e., Qadariyya), making humans the originators, and another that attributes them solely to God (Jabriyya). Maturidi points out that both extremes arise from considering only one side of the dual attribution found in revelation: actions are sometimes attributed to God and sometimes to servants. He then lists a series of dual attributes (e.g., misguidance and guidance, expansion and restriction) that are opposites and cannot coexist without a distinction in perspective. Since God's absolute attribution of these states to Himself would negate the possibility of opposite attributes being realized, it becomes necessary to distinguish between the creation (khalq) and the acquisition (kasb) of the act: God creates the act, and the servant acquires it. The proof is that when an act is called 'creation' (khalq), it implies mere origination from God; the same act, when considered from the human side, is understood as their act and acquisition. Shifting either perspective to a metaphorical interpretation would make the other likewise metaphorical, which would entail abandoning the literal truth of the Quranic attributes. The opposing schools—Jabriyya and Qadariyya—are thus refuted, with Maturidi referencing the tradition of cursing the Murji'a (who defer agency to God) and Qadariyya. The correct doctrine is 'justice' (al-'adl), which upholds both sides: God's creation of the act and human responsibility. This is supported by Quranic verses stating God's universal creation and power, and His justice in not wronging servants. Finally, a further proof is offered: some aspects of human actions are beyond human comprehension (like creation ex nihilo), while others are within their reach (like intention and choice). Thus, the act is not fully theirs from one viewpoint (creation) but is theirs from another (acquisition). The analogy of bringing something from non-existence to existence illustrates the creative aspect beyond human capacity.

Key Terms
العدل (al-'adl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Maturidi view compromises divine omnipotence or makes God the author of evil.
Correction: Maturidi distinguishes creation from acquisition: God creates all acts, but humans acquire them, preserving divine sovereignty and human responsibility. God's justice is not impugned because the act's evil aspect is not attributed to Him.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi call the correct doctrine that affirms both divine creation and human acquisition?
A) Jabr
B) Qadar
C) 'Adl
D) Kasb

Key Takeaway
The doctrine of 'adl (justice) upholds both God's creation of all acts and human acquisition, supported by Quranic verses and the inherent duality of human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a sin you committed today. The lesson teaches that God created its existence, but you acquired it by your choice. Does this truth make you feel more or less accountable? How can acknowledging both sides—God's creation and your choice—transform your repentance into a deeper reliance on His mercy?
?
When you face a difficulty that seems unfair, do you ever doubt that God is 'not unjust to His servants'? How does the Maturidi perspective, which affirms God's justice while recognizing aspects beyond human understanding, help you trust Him in that moment?
?
If you truly believed that every intention and effort you make is an acquisition from God's creation, would you live more intentionally? Identify one area where you tend to act carelessly, and commit to pausing before that action to thank God for enabling you to choose.

Divine Decree
beginner
5 min
Divine Creation and Human Acquisition
Maturidi defines divine creation as origination and human action as acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's distinction between divine creation (as origination) and human acquisition (kasb), and why both are real, not metaphorical.

Core Idea
God creates the act; the human acquires it—both are real.

Imam Maturidi begins by clarifying a foundational point: when we say an act is 'created' by God, it means origination. For the human, the same act is called 'acquisition.' This distinction prevents misunderstanding. In this passage, he sets up an analogy to show that treating either as metaphorical leads to inconsistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Maturidi defines divine creation and human acquisition side by side.
2
Identify the key terms
Pay attention to the terms 'خلق' (creation) and 'كسب' (acquisition) and how they are used.
These are central to Maturidi's theology.
3
Understand the analogy
Maturidi argues that if you treat one aspect metaphorically, the other must be treated similarly, leading to an inconsistency. Ask yourself why he makes this point.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction is important for avoiding both Jabriyya and Qadariyya extremes.
This leads into Lesson 2.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ان فعل الله تعالى في التحقيق خلقه، وكل ذلك لو أضيف إليه باسم الخلق لم يفهم منه في ذلك غير إنشاء، وفهم من الذي فهم من العبد فعله وكسبه نحو أن نقول : خلق الشرح والضيق، وخلق الضلال والاهتداء ونحو ذلك، فمثله الأول. ما لو جاز صرف أحد مع الوجهين عن حقيقة المفهوم أو صرفه إلى الأسباب أو الأحوال فالآخر مثله، وكل ذلك مجاز لا حقيقةٌ. ولذلك جاء مقابلة القولين : الجبرية والقدرية، وهذا معنى ما روى من لعن المرجئة والقدرية . إن المرجئة أرجأت الأفعال إلى الله ولم تجعلها للعبد، والقدرية أثبتتها الله على ما ينسب الخلق إلى الله تعالى، ولم تجعل الله فيها تدبيرا.
Verily, the act of Allah, the Exalted, in reality is His creation, and all of that if attributed to Him by the name 'creation' is not understood from it except origination. And it is understood from what is understood from the slave his act and his acquisition, such that we say: He created expansion and constriction, and He created misguidance and guidance, and the like. So the first is like it. If it is allowed to turn one of the two aspects from the reality of the understood meaning or to turn it to causes or states, then the other is like it, and all of that is metaphorical, not real. Therefore, the two opposing statements came: Jabriyya and Qadariyya. And this is the meaning of what has been narrated about cursing the Murji'a and Qadariyya. Indeed, the Murji'a deferred actions to Allah and did not make them for the slave, and the Qadariyya affirmed them for Allah in terms of attributing creation to Allah, and did not make Allah have disposal in them.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage defines the correct theological position on the nature of human actions, known as kasb (acquisition). The author begins by stating that in reality, God's act is His creation, and when attributed to Him as 'creation', it only means origination. For the human act, we understand it as both the human's act and his acquisition, as in phrases like 'He created expansion' or 'He created misguidance.' The first case (divine creation) is analogous to the second (human acquisition) in that both involve attribution. Then the author warns: if one were to take one of these two aspects metaphorically rather than literally, the other would be treated similarly, leading to inconsistency. This is why the two opposing schools emerged: Jabriyya (who deny human action any reality) and Qadariyya (who deny God's role in human actions). The author references a hadith about cursing the Murji'a and Qadariyya, explaining that the Murji'a attribute actions solely to God, while the Qadariyya affirm God's creation but deny His disposal. The correct view is that both aspects are real: God is the creator of the act, and the human acquires it.

Key Terms
خلق
كسب
مجاز
حقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates the act, the human cannot be held responsible; others think the human creates his own acts independently.
Correction: Maturidi affirms both: God creates the act (as origination) and the human acquires it, making responsibility compatible with divine creation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does God's 'creation' of an act mean?
A) God directly performs the act through the human
B) God originates the act into existence
C) The human creates the act independently
D) It is a metaphorical expression

Key Takeaway
God creates the act as origination, and the human acquires it—both are real aspects of the same act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you use the excuse 'Allah created it' to lessen your guilt? How does knowing that your acquisition (كسب) of the act is real and not metaphorical compel you to take full ownership of your choices today? Write one concrete way you will stop blaming circumstances and start repenting sincerely.
?
If you truly believe that Allah creates your every action including your faith, does that make your faith feel like a robotic imposition? How does the reality of your acquisition restore the personal, intimate nature of your relationship with Allah? What specific step will you take this week to actively acquire righteousness rather than passively wait for it?
?
Reflect on a time you felt proud of a good deed. Did you attribute it to yourself as if you were the ultimate source? This passage reminds you that Allah creates the act; your acquisition is real but dependent. How can you balance gratitude to Allah and personal effort without falling into self-congratulation? Commit to saying 'Allah created it, I acquired it' after every good deed you perform today.

Refuting Jabriyya and Qadariyya
Maturidi refutes Jabriyya and Qadariyya and explains the hadith about cursing the Murji'a and Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi refutes both Jabriyya and Qadariyya, and what the correct middle path is according to his theology.

Core Idea
Neither Jabriyya nor Qadariyya is correct; the truth is that God creates and the human acquires.

In the second part of the passage, Maturidi explicitly refers to the two extreme sects—Jabriyya and Qadariyya—and links them to a hadith about cursing the Murji'a and Qadariyya. He clarifies that the Murji'a (here meaning Jabriyya) deny human action, while the Qadariyya affirm creation to God but deny His disposal. The correct view holds both together.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the remainder of the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi connects the theoretical discussion to the sects.
2
Identify the two extremes
Find where Jabriyya and Qadariyya are mentioned and what they believe.
3
Understand the hadith reference
Maturidi cites a narration about cursing the Murji'a and Qadariyya. Consider how this supports the refutation.
4
Synthesize the middle path
Combine both lessons to see that the correct view affirms divine creation and human acquisition, avoiding both extremes.

The Definition of 'Adl and Its Proof from Human Actions
Maturidi defines 'adl and gives a proof from human actions' dual aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi defines 'adl as affirming both aspects of human actions and the proof based on the limits of human power.

Core Idea
Justice means affirming actions are from God as Creator and from humans as acquirers.

This passage from Imam Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid establishes the foundational concept of 'adl (justice). Maturidi defines 'adl not merely as God not being unjust, but as the affirmation of both divine creation and human acquisition in actions. He then presents a proof based on the observable aspects of human actions that are beyond our control and those within our intention. Let's read the passage and unpack its argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the Quranic verses cited at the beginning.
2
Identify the two aspects of 'adl
Maturidi defines 'adl as 'affirming both matters.' Find what these two matters are: that actions are from God as Creator and from humans as acquirers.
The verses support each aspect.
3
Analyze the proof from human actions
The proof is based on two aspects of actions: one beyond human control (e.g., coming into existence) and one within intention (e.g., movement). Understand how this shows actions belong to God in one way and to humans in another.
Consider the example of climbing stairs and being unable to return to the exact same step.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعدل هو القول بتحقيق الأمرين، ليكون الله موصوفاً بما وصف به نفسه محمودا به كما قال "خالق كل شيء" (الأنعام 102/6) ، وقال : "فهو على كل شيء قدير" (الأنعام 17/6)، وليكون عدلاً مفصلاً كما قال: "وما ربك بظلام للعبيد" (فصلت 46/41)، وقال: "ولولا فضل الله عليكم ورحمته لا تبعتم الشيطان إلا قليلا" (النساء 83/4). ثم الدليل على لزوم القول بهذا - مع ما فيما بينا كفاية - وجوه أحوال في أفعال العبد لا يبلغها أوهامهم ولا يقدرها عقولهم وأحوال فيها ينتهي إليها قصدهم وتبلغها عقولهم. فثبت أنها من الوجه الأول ليست لهم، ومن الوجه الثاني لهم . فالأول كتصوير خروج الشيء من العدم إلى الوجود وكأخذ الفعل من قدر الجو والمكان والحد الذي لو أحب أن يعود إليه ما أمكنه تلاقيه، والثاني نحو التحرك والسكون بالمنهى والمأمور به ثبت أن فعلهم من الوجه الأول ليس لهم، ومن الثاني لهم. ولو جاز تحقيق فعلهم من الوجه الأول على ظهور خروجه عن قصدهم - وجملتهم مختلفة مما ذكر ـ وعجزهم عن العود إلى مثله الجاز كون العالم على ما عليه بمن لا يقدر ولا يعلم ولا يعرف مقادير كل شيء، ويجوز أيضاً آيات - على ما هي عليه ـ بالبشر وإن لم يكن لهم بمثلها علم ولا عليها قدرة. فإذ لزمهم القول بالصانع والرسل بخروج الذي ذكرت عن وسع الخلق فمثله أفعال الخلق ؛ ولذلك قال الله سبحانه: ليس كمثله شيء (الشورى 11/42)، وأوجب أن تشابه الخلق من الوجه الذي قلت تماثل. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And justice is the statement affirming both matters, so that Allah is described as He described Himself, praised as He said: 'Creator of everything' (6:102), and He said: 'So He is over all things competent' (6:17), and so that He is a detailed justice as He said: 'And your Lord is not unjust to [His] servants' (41:46), and He said: 'And if not for the favor of Allah upon you and His mercy, you would have followed Satan, except for a few' (4:83). Then the proof for the necessity of this statement - besides what we have already explained being sufficient - are aspects of states in the actions of the slave that their imaginations do not reach nor their intellects measure, and states in which their intention terminates and their intellects attain. So it is established that they are from the first aspect not theirs, and from the second aspect theirs. So the first is like the portrayal of a thing's emergence from non-existence to existence, and like taking the action from the measure of the air, place, and limit that if he wished to return to it, he could not encounter it. And the second is like movement and stillness by the prohibited and commanded. So it is established that their action from the first aspect is not theirs, and from the second aspect theirs. And if it were allowed that their action from the first aspect is verified - despite its apparent exit from their intention - and their inability to return to the like of it - then it would be permissible for the world to be as it is from one who does not have power, knowledge, or knowledge of the measures of everything, and it would also be permissible for signs - as they are - to be from humans even though they have no knowledge of the like nor power over them. So since they are obliged to affirm the Maker and the messengers due to the exit of what I mentioned from the capacity of creation, similarly are the actions of creation. Therefore Allah said: 'There is nothing like Him' (42:11), and it necessitates that creation resemble from the aspect that I said similarity. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage defines 'adl (justice) as the affirmation of both aspects: that actions are from God as creation and from the human as acquisition. The author supports this with Quranic verses that describe God as Creator, all-powerful, and not unjust. Then he presents a proof: there are aspects of human actions that are beyond human imagination and control, and aspects that are within their intention and intellect. From the first aspect, actions are not theirs; from the second, they are. Examples include the emergence of a thing from non-existence (like creation) and the inability to return to an identical action (e.g., climbing stairs). The second aspect includes intentional movements. If actions from the first aspect were fully theirs despite being outside their intention, then one could argue that the world could exist without a powerful, knowing Creator, or that miracles could be performed by humans. Since we must affirm the Creator and messengers, similarly we affirm that human actions have a divine aspect. The verse 'There is nothing like Him' indicates that while there is similarity in one respect (the act of creation), there is no absolute likeness between Creator and creation.

خروج الشيء من العدم
تشابه
تماثل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's justice means humans have no free will or responsibility.
Correction: Maturidi shows that 'adl involves affirming both divine creation and human acquisition, so human responsibility is preserved.

Checkpoint

B) The moral quality of actions

D) The existence of prophets

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes 'adl as the affirmation of both divine creation and human acquisition in actions, supported by a proof from the limits of human power.

?

Second Proof from Good and Evil
Maturidi argues from human ignorance of moral quality to divine determination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's proof that human unawareness of the full moral quality of actions demonstrates a divine aspect beyond human control.

Core Idea
Human ignorance of moral outcomes reveals that actions are not entirely their own.

We now examine Maturidi's second proof for qadar. He points to a common experience: we intend to make our actions good, but often they emerge with a different moral quality than we expected. This gap between intention and outcome, Maturidi argues, shows that the action's moral character is not fully under our control. Let's read his argument carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow.
Notice the key terms: حسن (good), قبح (evil), تحسين (beautifying), تزيين (adorning).
2
Identify the key observation
Maturidi observes that people do not know the full extent of good or evil in their actions, yet they try to beautify them. The actions often turn out contrary to their intention.
This shows a gap between human intention and actual moral quality.
3
Understand the logical consequence
If actions were fully under human control while humans are ignorant of their moral quality, then ignorance of good and evil would be impossible. Therefore, actions are not entirely theirs.
Maturidi deduces that actions from this aspect are not solely human.
4
Consider the objection and response
An objector might say actions are good or evil in themselves. Maturidi responds: If that were true, then God is more deserving of the thing than itself, since everything originates from God.
This reinforces the divine aspect of actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا إنا نجد أفعال العباد تخرج على حسن وقبح لا يعلم أهلها أنها يبلغ في الحسن ذلك ولا في القبح، بل الهم عند أنفسهم في تحسينها وتزيينها، وهي تخرج على غير ذلك، بأن جعل أفعالهم على ما هي عليه ليست لهم؛ ولو جاز كونها على ذلك لهم ـ وهم لا يعرفون مبلغ الحسن والقبح ـ فإذا لا جهل بقبح الفعل ولا بحسنه . فثبت أن فعلهم من هذا الوجه ليس لهم. ولا قوة إلا بالله. اللهم إلا أن يقولوا: هي لأنفسها كانت كذلك. فإذا استقام حسن الفعل وقبحه بمنزلة الفعل نفسه، فالله تعالى أحق بالشيء من نفسه، إذ الشيء من الشيء.
And also we find the actions of servants emerge upon good and evil, their people not knowing that it reaches that [degree] in good or in evil. Rather, their concern in themselves is for beautifying and adorning them, and they emerge contrary to that. Thus, their actions are made as they are - they are not theirs. And if it were allowed that they are theirs in that way - while they do not know the extent of good and evil - then there would be no ignorance of the evil of the action nor of its good. So it is established that their action from this aspect is not theirs. And there is no power except with Allah. Unless they say: it was like that for itself. So if the goodness and evil of the action become established as equivalent to the action itself, then Allah is more deserving of the thing than itself, since the thing is from the thing.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage presents a second proof. Human actions emerge with a moral quality of good or evil, but the agents do not know the full extent of that goodness or evil. Their intention is to beautify and adorn their actions, yet they often turn out contrary to that intention. This shows that their actions are not entirely theirs; otherwise, if they had full control while ignorant of the moral outcome, there would be no ignorance of evil or good. The conclusion is that actions from this aspect are not solely the human's. The author then anticipates an objection: someone might say the action is good or evil in itself. If the moral quality is considered intrinsic to the action, then God is more deserving of the thing than itself, because everything originates from God. This reinforces the idea that the divine aspect is primary.

Key Terms
حسن
قبح
تحسين
تزيين
جهل
أحق
الشيء من الشيء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If humans are ignorant of the full moral quality of their actions, then they cannot be held responsible.
Correction: Maturidi uses ignorance not as an excuse but as evidence that actions are not entirely under human control, pointing to a divine aspect.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that human actions are not entirely theirs based on the example of good and evil?
A) Because humans do not know the full extent of good and evil
B) Because actions are always good
C) Because God determines all moral values
D) Because humans have no intention

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses the human inability to know the full moral quality of their own actions to prove that actions are not entirely under human control, pointing to a divine aspect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel confident that an action you are about to take is purely good, how does this passage challenge your certainty? Can you recall a specific time where you were sure you were doing good, only to later realize it had unintended evil consequences? How does that realization affect your reliance on your own judgment versus God's decree?
?
Maturidi argues that we do not even know the extent of good or evil in our actions. Are you willing to admit that you might be completely wrong about the moral quality of your most cherished deeds? If so, what does that mean for your sense of control over your fate?
?
The passage ends with 'God is more deserving of the thing than itself.' How can this truth transform the way you view your achievements and your failures? Are you ready to let go of the illusion that your actions are entirely yours, and instead surrender their outcome to the One who truly owns them?

God is the Creator of Everything: The Quranic Foundation
Maturidi cites Quran and infers God's exclusive creatorship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Quranic verse 'Creator of everything' to argue that God must be the creator of all acts, including human actions.

Core Idea
God's creation is universal; no act exists without Him.

Maturidi begins his refutation of the Mu'tazila by grounding his argument in a clear Quranic statement: God is the Creator of everything. This verse cannot be restricted or limited, and since human beings are not creators of their own acts, those acts must be attributed to God. Let us examine this foundational proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic citation
Notice how Maturidi begins with the general statement 'Creator of everything' (6:102) and argues it cannot be restricted to only some things.
This is a direct appeal to scripture.
2
Understand the logical move
He then argues that since the servant does not become a creator by his act, the act must be from another—i.e., God. This is a key step.
The negation of human creative power is crucial.
3
Connect to the broader debate
Consider how this simple argument challenges the Mu'tazila position that humans create their own actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استعمال العموم بقوله : خالق كل شيء ﴾ [الأنعام، ١٠٢/٦]، إذ لا سبيل إلى وجود خلق كل شيء باسم الخاصية له، أو يلزم القول بالقياس من الوجه الذي ذكر . ثم لم يصر العبد بفعله خالقاً ، ثبت أنه بغيره . مع ما إذ كان سبيل معرفة الفاعل إنما هو بآثار الفعل . ثم كان الإيمان من أحسن الأفعال في العقول وأنور الأشياء وأتمها وأجلّها قدرًا وأثبتها لمرضاته. فلو قلنا: إن الله غير خالق له دخل علينا أمران في ذلك أحدهما تفضيل من يطيع الله بالإيمان وغيره على الله بما خلق من الأقذار والأنتان والخبائث والقبائح من الجواهر؛ مع ما كان ما حَسُن من الجواهر لا يبلغ قدر الذي ذكر من [الإيمان و] العبادات في الحسن والخير. وإذا كان كذلك - ومعلوم تفاضل الفاضلين بتفاضل أفعالهم - أوجب ذلك فضل العبد على الله في الفعل والخلق. وهذا بالمعتزلة أولى، لأنهم زعموا أن فعل الكفر قبيح شر من جميع الوجوه، وليس كذلك أمر القردة والخنازير، فمثله فعل الإيمان [خير] من جميع جواهر الحسان ولا قوة إلا بالله . والثاني أن ثوابه إذ حُسنه حستى وحسن الايمان عقلي، وما حسن في الحس دون الذي يحسن في العقل، إذ قد يجوز انقلاب مثله على ما مربيانه، ولا يجوز انقلاب الآخر. وإذا كان كذلك فيقتصر الجزاء على قدر المجزي [به]، والله وعد جزاء الحسنة بعشر أمثالها ، ثبت أن خلق فعل الإيمان حسنا الله ولا قوة إلا بالله. وبعد، فإن الله تعالى ذم الذين يحبون أن يُحمدوا بما لم يفعلوا، ثم ألزم عباده الشكر له على الإيمان، والحمد لله على الإنعام؛ لم يجز أن يكون غير خالق لذلك فيَستَأدى الحمد على ما لم يفعله، والشكر على ما لم يُسند إلى أحد به. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
The use of the general [statement] by His saying: 'Creator of everything' (Quran 6:102), for there is no way to the existence of the creation of everything by the name of particularity for Him, or else the saying of analogy from the mentioned aspect would be necessary. Then, since the servant did not become a creator by his act, it is established that it [the act] is by another. Moreover, since the way of knowing the agent is only through the traces of the act, and faith is among the best acts in intellects, the most luminous of things, the most perfect, the most exalted in rank, and the most established for His pleasure. So if we were to say that God is not its creator, two matters would enter upon us in that: one of them is preferring the one who obeys God through faith and other things over God, because of what He has created of filths, stinks, foul things, and ugly things among substances, while what is good among substances does not reach the measure of what was mentioned of faith and worship in goodness and virtue. And if that is so—and it is known that the superiority of the two excellent ones is by the superiority of their acts—then that would necessitate the servant's superiority over God in act and creation. And this is more appropriate to the Mu'tazila, because they claimed that the act of unbelief is ugly and evil in all respects, yet the matter of apes and pigs is not so, so likewise the act of faith is better than all beautiful substances—and there is no power but in God. The second [matter] is that its reward—since its goodness and the goodness of faith are rational—and what is good in sensation is not like what is good in intellect, for it is possible for the like of it to change based on what we have mentioned, but it is not possible for the other to change. And if that is so, then recompense is limited to the measure of what is recompensed for, and God has promised the recompense of a good deed by ten times its like; thus it is established that God created the act of faith as good—and there is no power but in God. Moreover, God Almighty blames those who love to be praised for what they did not do, then He obligated His servants to thank Him for faith and to praise Him for favor; it is not permissible that He be not the creator of that, so that He would require praise for what He did not do, and thankfulness for what was not attributed to anyone. And there is no power but in God.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila position that God does not create human acts, specifically acts of faith and disobedience. The author, Maturidi, begins by referencing the Quranic verse 'Creator of everything' (6:102), arguing that this general statement cannot be restricted to a particular class of things without evidence, nor can it be limited by analogy. He then states that the servant does not become a creator by his act, so the act must be from another—i.e., God. The way to know an agent is through the effects of the act, and faith is one of the best acts in intellect. If God were not the creator of faith, two problems follow: First, it would mean preferring the obedient servant over God, because God created filth and ugly substances while the servant's act of faith is better than all beautiful substances; thus the servant would be superior in act and creation. This contradiction is especially problematic for the Mu'tazila, who claim that unbelief is absolutely evil, but then they must admit that faith is better than God's own beautiful creations. Second, if faith's goodness is rational and not merely sensory, then its reward must be proportional to its rational goodness, and God has promised tenfold reward; this implies that God created the act of faith as good. He then reinforces the argument by noting that God blames those who love praise for what they did not do; if God were not the creator of faith, He would be asking for praise for something He did not do, which is impossible. Therefore, God must be the creator of all acts, including human actions.

Key Terms
خالق
فعل
خاصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse 'Creator of everything' excludes human acts because humans seem to create their own actions.
Correction: Maturidi shows the verse is universal and humans are not creators, so all acts are God's creation.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi use as the primary evidence for God being the creator of all acts?
A) Rational argument alone
B) The Quranic verse 'Creator of everything'
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Analogy from nature

Key Takeaway
God's universal creatorship includes human acts; denying this contradicts the Quran and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every act you do is created by God, how does that change the way you see your own 'achievements'? Will you thank Him more humbly before you claim credit?
?
You often exercise your will without thinking of God. How can the knowledge that your very act of writing, speaking, or thinking is created by Him transform your consciousness? Will you pause before your next action to acknowledge His creation?
?
If you cannot create even a single act, what does that say about your pride? Will you surrender your sense of self-creation today and live in constant dependence on Allah?

The Absurdity of Human Superiority in Creation
Maturidi deduces human superiority if God is not creator of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that if God does not create acts of faith, it would imply that the human believer is superior to God in creating good things.

Core Idea
Denying divine creation of good acts exalts humans above God.

Maturidi now draws out a startling consequence of the Mu'tazila denial of divine creation. If God is not the creator of the best act—faith—then the believer's act of faith would be better than anything God has created, including beautiful substances. This would imply the believer is superior to God in the quality of creation, an absurd and blasphemous conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the premise
Notice that Maturidi establishes that faith is the best act in intellect and most luminous.
This sets up the comparison.
2
Follow the comparison
He compares faith to the created substances God makes, like filth and ugly things. Faith is better than any beautiful substance.
The contrast is stark.
3
Understand the conclusion
If the servant's act is better than God's created objects, and knowing the superior one is known by his act, then the servant would be superior to God in act and creation.
This is the absurdity.
4
Note the Mu'tazila irony
Maturidi points out that the Mu'tazila themselves consider unbelief absolutely evil but apes/pigs are not considered that evil, so faith is even better.
This strengthens the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

In what subtle ways do you exalt yourself above God in your daily life—perhaps by thinking you are better than others, or by relying on your own plans instead of trusting God? Can you identify one specific attitude or action today that reflects this tendency and commit to turning it into humble submission?
?
The passage describes faith as 'the most luminous of things, the most perfect, and the most exalted in rank.' If this is true, then your faith is the most valuable thing you possess. How much time and effort do you invest in nurturing it compared to your worldly pursuits? What concrete change can you make this week to prioritize your faith over other concerns?

The Rational Goodness of Faith and the Impossibility of False Praise
Maturidi uses reward proportionality and divine praise to prove God creates faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's arguments that faith's rational goodness entails divine creation, and that God cannot demand gratitude for what He did not create.

Core Idea
Faith's rational excellence proves God created it; otherwise praise would be false.

Maturidi completes his refutation with two additional points. First, faith's goodness is rational, not merely sensory, and its reward is proportional—God promised tenfold, which only makes sense if He created it. Second, God condemns those who love praise for what they did not do; yet He commands gratitude for faith. If He didn't create it, He would be praising Himself falsely. Both arguments reinforce that God must be the creator of all acts, including human faith.

Guided Path
1
Understand the reward argument
Maturidi argues that faith's goodness is rational, unlike sensory goodness. Sensory things can change, but rational goodness is stable. God promised reward for good deeds; this implies God created the goodness of faith.
The argument uses the principle that reward corresponds to the act's goodness.
2
Examine the praise argument
God blames those who want praise for what they didn't do. Yet He commands thanks for faith. If He didn't create faith, He would be like those He blames.
This is a moral contradiction.
3
Connect both points
Together, these arguments show that attributing faith to human creation alone leads to theological and moral inconsistencies.

استعمال العموم بقوله : خالق كل شيء ﴾ [الأنعام، ١٠٢/٦]، إذ لا سبيل إلى وجود خلق كل شيء باسم الخاصية له، أو يلزم القول بالقياس من الوجه الذي ذكر . ثم لم يصر العبد بفعله خالقاً ، ثبت أنه بغيره . مع ما إذ كان سبيل معرفة الفاعل إنما هو بآثار الفعل . ثم كان الإيمان من أحسن الأفعال في العقول وأنور الأشياء وأتمها وأجلّها قدرًا وأثبتها لمرضاته. فلو قلنا: إن الله غير خالق له دخل علينا أمران في ذلك أحدهما تفضيل من يطيع الله بالإيمان وغيره على الله بما خلق من الأقذار والأنتان والخبائث والقبائح من الجواهر؛ مع ما كان ما حَسُن من الجواهر لا يبلغ قدر الذي ذكر من [الإيمان و] العبادات في الحسن والخير. وإذا كان كذلك - ومعلوم تفاضل الفاضلين بتفاضل أفعالهم - أوجب ذلك فضل العبد على الله في الفعل والخلق. وهذا بالمعتزلة أولى، لأنهم زعموا أن فعل الكفر قبيح شر من جميع الوجوه، وليس كذلك أمر القردة والخنازير، فمثله فعل الإيمان [خير] من جميع جواهر الحسان ولا قوة إلا بالله . والثاني أن ثوابه إذ حُسنه حستى وحسن الايمان عقلي، وما حسن في الحس دون الذي يحسن في العقل، إذ قد يجوز انقلاب مثله على ما مربيانه، ولا يجوز انقلاب الآخر. وإذا كان كذلك فيقتصر الجزاء على قدر المجزي [به]، والله وعد جزاء الحسنة بعشر أمثالها ، ثبت أن خلق فعل الإيمان حسنا الله ولا قوة إلا بالله. وبعد، فإن الله تعالى ذم الذين يحبون أن يُحمدوا بما لم يفعلوا، ثم ألزم عباده الشكر له على الإيمان، والحمد لله على الإنعام؛ لم يجز أن يكون غير خالق لذلك فيَستَأدى الحمد على ما لم يفعله، والشكر على ما لم يُسند إلى أحد به. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
The use of the general [statement] by His saying: 'Creator of everything' (Quran 6:102), for there is no way to the existence of the creation of everything by the name of particularity for Him, or else the saying of analogy from the mentioned aspect would be necessary. Then, since the servant did not become a creator by his act, it is established that it [the act] is by another. Moreover, since the way of knowing the agent is only through the traces of the act, and faith is among the best acts in intellects, the most luminous of things, the most perfect, the most exalted in rank, and the most established for His pleasure. So if we were to say that God is not its creator, two matters would enter upon us in that: one of them is preferring the one who obeys God through faith and other things over God, because of what He has created of filths, stinks, foul things, and ugly things among substances, while what is good among substances does not reach the measure of what was mentioned of faith and worship in goodness and virtue. And if that is so—and it is known that the superiority of the two excellent ones is by the superiority of their acts—then that would necessitate the servant's superiority over God in act and creation. And this is more appropriate to the Mu'tazila, because they claimed that the act of unbelief is ugly and evil in all respects, yet the matter of apes and pigs is not so, so likewise the act of faith is better than all beautiful substances—and there is no power but in God. The second [matter] is that its reward—since its goodness and the goodness of faith are rational—and what is good in sensation is not like what is good in intellect, for it is possible for the like of it to change based on what we have mentioned, but it is not possible for the other to change. And if that is so, then recompense is limited to the measure of what is recompensed for, and God has promised the recompense of a good deed by ten times its like; thus it is established that God created the act of faith as good—and there is no power but in God. Moreover, God Almighty blames those who love to be praised for what they did not do, then He obligated His servants to thank Him for faith and to praise Him for favor; it is not permissible that He be not the creator of that, so that He would require praise for what He did not do, and thankfulness for what was not attributed to anyone. And there is no power but in God.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila position that God does not create human acts, specifically acts of faith and disobedience. The author, Maturidi, begins by referencing the Quranic verse 'Creator of everything' (6:102), arguing that this general statement cannot be restricted to a particular class of things without evidence, nor can it be limited by analogy. He then states that the servant does not become a creator by his act, so the act must be from another—i.e., God. The way to know an agent is through the effects of the act, and faith is one of the best acts in intellect. If God were not the creator of faith, two problems follow: First, it would mean preferring the obedient servant over God, because God created filth and ugly substances while the servant's act of faith is better than all beautiful substances; thus the servant would be superior in act and creation. This contradiction is especially problematic for the Mu'tazila, who claim that unbelief is absolutely evil, but then they must admit that faith is better than God's own beautiful creations. Second, if faith's goodness is rational and not merely sensory, then its reward must be proportional to its rational goodness, and God has promised tenfold reward; this implies that God created the act of faith as good. He then reinforces the argument by noting that God blames those who love praise for what they did not do; if God were not the creator of faith, He would be asking for praise for something He did not do, which is impossible. Therefore, God must be the creator of all acts, including human actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think faith's goodness comes from human choice alone, so reward is deserved by humans, not God.
Correction: Maturidi argues that reward is proportional to the goodness created by God; if humans created it, reward would be infinite.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that faith's rational goodness implies God created it?
A) Because rational goodness never changes
B) Because God promised a specific reward for it
C) Because humans cannot create anything good
D) Because faith is known by revelation

Key Takeaway
Faith's rational goodness and God's demand for gratitude both require that God is the creator of the act of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever secretly credited yourself for your own faith, feeling proud that you 'chose' to believe? Maturidi's argument shows that even the goodness of your faith is created by God. How will you change your gratitude tomorrow when you wake up with imān in your heart?
?
When you thank God for something good in your life, do you truly believe He is the sole creator of that good, including your ability to recognize it? This passage says God would be unjust to demand thanks for what He didn't do. Search your heart: is there any area where you thank God while secretly believing you partly earned it?
?
God condemns those who love praise for what they didn't do. Now think: do you ever seek admiration from others for your religious devotion—your prayers, charity, or knowledge? If God alone creates those acts, what right do you have to seek praise? Commit tonight to one specific way you will deflect praise back to God.
